Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
6 min
Valid Capital for Mufawadha and 'Inan Partnerships
Stating that only gold, silver, tibr, and fulus are valid capital; rebutting Malik's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for valid capital in mufawadha and 'inan partnerships and explain the reasoning behind excluding commodities.

Core Idea
Only monetary items (gold, silver, tibr, fulus) qualify as capital to prevent profit from unguaranteed property.

When forming a mufawadha or 'inan partnership, the capital contributed must be of a specific nature. The Hanafi school strictly limits capital to monetary items—minted gold and silver, unminted bullion (tibr) if customarily used as money, and current copper coins (fulus). This restriction avoids the prohibited 'profit from what one did not guarantee' (ribḥ mā lam yaḍman). In contrast, Imam Malik permits commodities of the same type, arguing they resemble money as known capital. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi stance, the Maliki objection, and the intra-Hanafi differences over fulus and tibr.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on valid capital
Identify what types of assets are allowed: the two metals (naqdayn), tibr (if customary), and fulus (if current). Note that commodities (urud) are excluded.
The base ruling is in the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik allows partnership with commodities (urud) and measured/weighed items of the same type, because they are known capital analogous to money.
Also note the exception for mudaraba, which Malik restricts to the textual source.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Maliki proof is qiyas: a partnership with known capital resembles one with money, so commodities should be allowed. Mudaraba is excluded because analogy fails there.
Malik treats partnership and mudaraba differently.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal focuses on ربح ما لم يضمن: if each partner sells his commodity capital, the prices may differ, and the partner receiving a higher price profits from his partner's property without guaranteed, which is forbidden. With money, the first transaction is a purchase on credit (guaranteed), avoiding this issue.
Also note: sale of one's property for partnership in its price is invalid, but purchase for partnership in the purchased item is valid.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical result: a partnership with commodities is valid in Maliki but invalid in Hanafi. The Hanafi view also includes intra-madhhab discussions on tibr and fulus, with the operative fatwa permitting tibr and fulus when customary.
Al-Asbijabi and the author of Kanz adopt the permissibility of fulus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشركة لا العرض ولا تصح مفاوضة وعنان بغير النقدين والتبر والفلوس ولو باع كل
وقال مالك : تجوز بالعروض والمكيل والموزون أيضاً إذا كان الجنس واحداً لأنها عقدت على رأس مال معلوم فأشبه النقود بخلاف المضاربة لأن القياس يأباها لما فيها من ربح ما لم يضمن فيقتصر على مورد الشرع. ولنا أنه يؤدي إلى ربح ما لم يضمن لأنه إذا باع كل واحد منهما رأس ماله وتفاضل الثمنان فما يستحقه أحدهما من الزيادة في مال صاحبه ربح ما لم يملك وما لم يضمن بخلاف الدراهم والدنانير لأن ثمن ما لا تتعين فكان يشتريه فى ذمته إذ هي . ربح ما ضمن ولأن أول التصرف في العرض البيع وفي النقود الشراء وبيع أحدهما ما له على أن يكون الآخر شريكاً في ثمنه لا يجوز، وشراء أحدهما شيئاً بماله على أن يكون المبيع بينه وبين غيره جائز وجعل المصنف التبر كالنقدين رواية كتاب الصرف بناء على أنه لا يتعين بالتعيين حتى لا ينفسخ العقد بهلاكه قبل التسليم. وفي الجامع الصغير : لا تكون المفاوضة بمثاقيل ذهب أو فضة ومراده التبر، فعلى هذه الرواية التبر سلعة ويتعين بالتعيين فلا يصلح رأس مال في المضاربات والشركات. وصححه في الهداية لأنها وإن خلقت للتجارة في الأصل لكن الثمنية تختص بالضرب المخصوص عند ذلك لا يصرف إلى شيء آخر ظاهراً إلا أن يجري التعامل باستعمالها ثمناً فينزل التعامل بمنزلة الضرب فتكون ثمناً وتصلح رأس المال .اهـ. فيحمل ما في الكتاب على ما إذا جرى التعامل باستعمال التبر ثمناً وهو أولى من حمله على الرواية الضعيفة والتبر ما ليس بمضروب الفضة والذهب وأطلق الفلوس وأراد بها الرائجة لأنها تروج رواج الأثمان فألحقت بها قالوا: هذا قول محمد لأنها ملحقة بالنقود عنده حتى لا تتعين بالتعيين، ولا يجوز بيع اثنين بواحد بأعيانهما على ما عرف. أما عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لا تجوز الشركة والمضاربة بها لأن ثمنيتها تتبدل ساعة فساعة وتصير سلعة. وروي عن أبي يوسف مثل قول محمد والأول أقيس وأظهر، والأصح أنها جائزة بالفلوس عندهما أيضاً لأنها أثمان باصطلاح الكل فلا تبطل ما لم يصطلح على ضده ؛ ذكره الأسبيجابي. ولذا اختاره في الكتاب. وشمل قوله بغير
The partnership is not on commodities, and mufawadha and 'inan are not valid except with the two metals (gold and silver), bullion, and fulus, even if each sells. Malik said: It is permissible with commodities and measured and weighed items as well, if the type is one, because it is contracted upon known capital, so it resembles money, unlike mudaraba because analogy rejects it due to the profit from what was not guaranteed, so it is limited to the textual source. For us: it leads to profit from what was not guaranteed, because if each of them sells his capital and the two prices differ, then what one of them receives of the increase in his partner's property is profit from what he did not own and what he did not guarantee, unlike dirhams and dinars because what is sold is non-specific, so he buys it in his obligation; thus it is profit from what was guaranteed. And because the first transaction in a commodity is sale, while in money it is purchase, and selling one's property on condition that the other is a partner in its price is not permissible, but buying something with his property on condition that the sold item is between him and someone else is permissible. The author treats bullion (tibr) like the two metals (gold/silver) according to the narration of Kitab al-Sarf, based on it not being specified by designation, so that the contract is not rescinded by its destruction before delivery. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: mufawadha is not valid with weighed quantities of gold or silver, and by this he means tibr. According to this narration, tibr is a commodity and becomes specified by designation, so it is not valid as capital in mudaraba and partnerships. This was corrected in al-Hidayah because, although they were created for trade originally, monetary value is specific to the particular minted coin; at that time, it is not outwardly exchanged for something else unless there is a custom using it as money, then custom takes the place of minting, so it becomes money and is valid as capital. End quote. Thus what is in the book (Kanz) is interpreted as when there is a custom of using tibr as money, which is better than relying on the weak narration. Tibr is unminted silver or gold. He used fulus in an absolute sense, meaning the current ones because they circulate like money, so they are annexed to it. They said: This is the view of Muhammad, because with him they are annexed to money such that they are not specified by designation, and it is not permissible to sell two for one of their specific types as is known. As for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, partnership and mudaraba are not permissible with them because their monetary value changes from moment to moment and they become a commodity. It is related from Abu Yusuf a view like Muhammad's, and the first is more analogical and apparent, but the correct view is that it is permissible with fulus according to both of them as well, because they are money by the convention of all, so it does not invalidate as long as they have not agreed otherwise. Al-Asbijabi mentioned this, and therefore it was chosen in the book (Kanz). And his statement 'with other than' includes...
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and an intra-Hanafi dispute about the valid capital for mufawadha and 'inan partnerships. The Hanafi position is that only the two metals (gold and silver) in minted form, as well as unminted bullion (tibr) when it is customarily used as money, and current fulus (copper coins) are valid as capital. The reason is to avoid 'profit from what was not guaranteed' (ربح ما لم يضمن). The commentator explains that if commodities were allowed, the sale of each partner's capital could result in differing prices, and the increase in one partner's share would be profit from something he did not own or guarantee. In contrast, with coins, the transaction is a purchase in one's liability, ensuring guarantee. The author al-Marghinani (in al-Hidayah) corrects the view about tibr: though created for trade, if it is customarily used as money, it becomes equivalent to minted coins. For fulus, the text reports that Muhammad al-Shaybani considers them as money and not specified by designation, so they are valid. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf initially considered them as commodities because their value fluctuates, but a later narration from Abu Yusuf aligns with Muhammad, and the correct view according to al-Asbijabi is that they are valid as long as they are commonly accepted as money. The passage also addresses the position of Imam Malik, who allows partnership with commodities of the same type because they are known capital, analogous to money. The Hanafi response is that this leads to profit without guarantee, and the first transaction in commodities is sale (which transfers ownership before partnership), whereas for money it is purchase (which creates partnership from the start).

Key Terms
نقدين (naqdayn): The two metals: gold and silver in minted form (dinars and dirhams).
تبر (tibr): Unminted gold or silver; considered a commodity unless custom treats it as money.
فلوس (fulūs): Copper coins; current ones that circulate as money are valid capital.
ربح ما لم يضمن (ribḥ mā lam yaḍman): Profit from something one did not guarantee; a prohibited form of earning in partnerships.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid capital for a mufawadha partnership?
A) One hundred dirhams of minted silver
B) Ten bushels of wheat of identical quality
C) A cow and a sheep
D) A promissory note

Key Takeaway
Only monetary items (gold, silver, tibr, fulus under conditions) qualify as partnership capital to prevent profit from unguaranteed property.

Partnership After Mixing Goods: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad al-Shaybani
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partnership after mixing goods of the same type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a partnership after mixing goods of the same type and explain the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Mixing goods of the same type does not create a valid partnership according to the relied-upon Hanafi view; each retains his own goods.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether mixing commodities (urud) of the same type before forming a partnership contract validates the partnership. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between valid and invalid partnership structures according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the position of Abu Yusuf (and the apparent transmission from Abu Hanifa): the partnership is not valid; each partner retains his own goods with profit/loss per his share.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view.
2
Identify the opposing view
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's view: the partnership is valid if the mixture is of one type (fungible goods).
Muhammad's view is a minority opinion within the school.
3
Analyze the proof for each view
Abu Yusuf argues that goods become specific by designation (yata'ayyan bil-ta'yin), so they remain pure commodities. Muhammad argues that mixing same-type goods creates a fungible mixture, allowing partnership.
The key distinction is fungibility (mithli) vs. non-fungibility (qimi).
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical consequence is whether unequal profit shares can be stipulated: Abu Yusuf disallows, Muhammad allows.
This affects how partners structure their agreement.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Abu Yusuf's view is the relied-upon position because it is the zahir al-riwayah (apparent transmission) from Abu Hanifa.
Later Hanafi works like al-Hidayah follow this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النقدين المكيل والموزون والمعدود المتقارب ولا خلاف فيه بيننا قبل الخلط لأنها عروض محضة، وكذا إن خلطا ثم اشتركا عند أبي يوسف فلكل منهما متاعه بحصة ربحه ووضيعته . وعند محمد تصح وتصير شركة عقد إذا كان المخلوط جنساً واحداً. وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر في اشتراط التفاضل في الربح فعند أبي يوسف لا تصح، وعند محمد تلزم، وقول أبي يوسف هو ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة لأنه يتعين بالتعيين فكان عرضاً محضاً. ولو اختلفا جنساً كالحنطة والشعير والزيت والسمن فخلطا لا تنعقد الشركة بها بالاتفاق. والفرق لمحمد أن المخلوط من جنس واحد من ذوات الأمثال، ومن جنسين من ذوات القيم فتتمكن الجهالة في العروض، وإذا لم تصح الشركة فحكم الخلط سيأتي في كتاب الوديعة.
And similarly if they mixed then entered partnership: according to Abu Yusuf each of them retains his own goods with his share of profit and loss. According to Muhammad it is valid and becomes a partnership by contract if the mixture is of one type. The fruit of the difference appears in stipulating disparity in profit: according to Abu Yusuf it is not valid, according to Muhammad it is binding. The statement of Abu Yusuf is the apparent transmission from Abu Hanifa because it becomes specific by assignment so it was a pure commodity. And if they differed in type such as wheat and barley, oil and clarified butter, and they mixed, the partnership is not valid by agreement. The distinction for Muhammad is that the mixture of one type is from fungible things, and of two types from non-fungible things, so ambiguity arises in commodities. And if the partnership is not valid, the ruling of the mixture will come in the Book of Deposit.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the validity of a partnership (shirkat al-'inan) when the partners first mix their commodities (urud) of the same type before making the contract. According to Abu Yusuf, each partner retains his own goods and the share of profit and loss corresponds to his share in the mixed goods; the partnership is not valid. According to Muhammad, if the mixture is of one type (e.g., both wheat), the partnership becomes valid as a contract. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is in the permissibility of stipulating unequal profit shares: Abu Yusuf disallows it, Muhammad upholds it. Abu Yusuf's view is the zahir al-riwayah (apparent transmission) from Abu Hanifa, because the goods become specific by designation (yata'ayyan bil-ta'yin) and thus remain as pure commodities. If the goods are of different types (e.g., wheat and barley), both agree the partnership is invalid. Muhammad's distinction is that one-type mixtures involve fungible goods (dhawat al-amthal), which can be equalized, whereas two-type mixtures involve non-fungible goods (dhawat al-qiyam), leading to ambiguity. If the partnership is invalid, the ruling of the mixture is deferred to the Book of Deposit (Kitab al-Wadi'ah).

Key Terms
عروض (urud): Commodities other than dirhams and dinars.
ذوات الأمثال (dhawat al-amthal): Fungible goods that can be replaced by equivalents (e.g., wheat, barley).
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted position from the core books of Imam Muhammad (the six books).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (Abu Yusuf), if two partners mix goods of the same type (e.g., both wheat) and then form a partnership contract, what is the ruling?
A) The partnership is valid and profit can be unequal.
B) The partnership is not valid; each retains his own goods.
C) The partnership is valid only if they sell half of each other's goods first.
D) The partnership is invalid if they mix different types but valid if same type.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, mixing commodities of the same type before a partnership does not transform them into valid partnership capital; each partner retains his own goods according to the relied-upon view.

Condition that Capital Be Present at Time of Purchase
States that capital must be present at the time of purchase, not at the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition regarding the presence of capital in a Hanafi partnership and identify the precise timing (at purchase, not at contract) required for validity.

Core Idea
Capital must be present at the time of purchase, not at the contract.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym expands on the Kanz al-Daqa'iq by clarifying an implicit condition: the capital in a partnership must be physically present. Although the matn does not mention it, later sources like al-Quniyah and al-Bazzaziyyah affirm this condition as necessary for validity. The crucial distinction is that the presence is required at the moment of purchase (waqt al-shira'), not at the moment of forming the partnership contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Gap in the Matn
Notice that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not explicitly restrict the capital to be present. The commentator Ibn Nujaym flags this as an omission that must be addressed for a valid partnership.
This is typical of expansion (istidrak) in later Hanafi works.
2
State the Condition from Later Sources
Ibn Nujaym cites al-Quniyah and al-Bazzaziyyah to establish that the capital must be present (hadir). Without this condition, the partnership contract is invalid.
The condition applies to both 'inan and mufawadah.
3
Distinguish the Timing
Al-Bazzaziyyah clarifies that the requirement is at the time of purchase, not at the time of the contract. This is the key nuance: the partnership can be contracted even if the capital is absent, as long as it is present when a purchase is made using partnership funds.
This allows flexibility in forming the partnership.
4
Apply the Rule to Examples
Work through the example from al-Quniyah: if one partner's capital is absent at the contract, but he delivers it after the meeting separates, the partnership becomes valid upon delivery when the partner uses both capitals to buy. Similarly, the agent who receives capital can prove that he brought the capital at purchase.
Delivery after the contract does not automatically validate; it must be before purchase.
5
Differentiate Genuine Partnership from Loan
The al-Dhakhirah case shows that if the arrangement is a loan with profit-sharing, it is not a partnership, and all profit goes to the borrower. The condition of capital presence is irrelevant there because the transaction is not a valid partnership.
This highlights the importance of proper contract formation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يقيد المصنف المال بالحضرة ولا بد منه قال في القنية : عقدا شركة عنان بالدنانير ورأس مال أحدهما غائب لا تصح ولو دفعه بعد الافتراق عن المجلس ليشتري الشريك بالمالين على ذلك العقد تنعقد الشركة بالدفع .اهـ. وفي البزازية : لا تصح بمال غائب أو دين ولا بد من أن يكون المال حاضراً مفاوضة كانت أو عناناً. وأراد عند عقد الشراء لا عند عقد الشركة فإنه لو لم يوجد عند عقدها تجوز ألا ترى أنه لو دفع إلى رجل ألفاً وقال اخرج مثلها أو اشتر بها وبع والحاصل بيننا أنصافاً ، ولم يكن المال حاضراً وقت الشركة فبرهن المأمور على أنه فعل ذلك وأحضر المال وقت الشراء جاز اهـ. وفي الذخيرة : إذا قال لغيره اقرضني ألفاً أتجر بها ويكون الربح بيننا فأقرضه ألفاً فاتجر بها وربح فالربح كله للمستقرض لا شركة للمقرض فيه، ولو دفع إلى رجل ألفاً وقال اشتر بها بيني وبينك نصفين والربح لنا والوضيعة علينا فهلك المال قبل أن يشتري فلا ضمان عليه وهذا ليس بقرض وإنما هو شركة، ولو اشترى بالمال هلك المال فعلى الآمر ضمان نصف المال وعلى المشتري نصف ذلك اهـ .
The author did not restrict the capital to be present, but it is necessary. It is stated in al-Quniyah: If two people contract a partnership of 'inan with dinars and the capital of one is absent, it is not valid. But if he pays it after separation from the gathering so that the partner buys with the two capitals on that contract, the partnership becomes valid by payment. In al-Bazzaziyyah: It is not valid with absent capital or debt, and the capital must be present whether it is mufawadah or 'inan. What is meant is at the time of purchase not at the time of contract, for if it is not present at the contract it is permissible. Do you not see that if he gives a man a thousand and says 'bring out the like of it' or 'buy with it and sell and the proceeds are between us half and half', and the capital was not present at the time of partnership, but the agent proves that he did that and brought the capital at the time of purchase, it is valid. In al-Dhakhirah: If he says to another 'lend me a thousand to trade with and the profit is between us', and he lends him a thousand, he trades and profits, then all the profit is for the borrower, no partnership for the lender. And if he gives a man a thousand and says 'buy with it between me and you half and half, profit for us and loss upon us', and the money perishes before he buys, then no liability on him, and this is not a loan but a partnership. And if he buys with the money and the money perishes, then the commander guarantees half the money and the buyer guarantees half.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage supplements the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) by noting that the author did not explicitly mention the condition that the capital must be present (hadir). The commentator Ibn Nujaym asserts that this condition is necessary. He cites al-Quniyah: if two people contract a shirkat al-'inan with dinars and one partner's capital is absent, the contract is invalid; but if he delivers it after the gathering has separated and the partner then buys with both capitals, the partnership becomes valid upon delivery. Al-Bazzaziyyah confirms that the capital must be present, but clarifies that the requirement is for the time of purchase (waqt al-shira'), not the time of contract. So if the capital is not present at the contract but is brought at the time of purchase, it is valid. An example: a man gives another a thousand and says 'bring out a similar thousand' or 'buy with it and sell, the proceeds between us equally'; the agent must prove he did so and brought the capital at purchase. Al-Dhakhirah adds two cases: (1) a loan disguised as partnership—if someone lends money for trade with a profit-sharing condition, all profit goes to the borrower because the loan is invalid as partnership; (2) a genuine partnership where the money is given to buy jointly—if the money is lost before purchase, there is no liability on the agent; if lost after purchase, the loss is shared between the commander and the agent.

Key Terms
حاضر (hadir): Capital that is physically present at the time of purchase.
شركة العقد (shirkat al-'aqd): A partnership formed by a contract (e.g., 'inan or mufawadah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When must the capital be present for a partnership (shirkat al-'inan) to be valid?
A) At the time of the contract.
B) At the time of purchase (shira').
C) At the time of profit distribution.
D) At the time of the initial meeting.

Key Takeaway
Capital must be physically present at the time of purchase, not at the contract, for a Hanafi partnership to be valid.

The Legal Stratagem (Hila) for Validating Commodity-Based Partnership
Explains the hila and the dispute on equal valuation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the legal stratagem for making a partnership with commodities valid and identify the Hanafi disagreement on value equality.

Core Idea
Selling half of each partner's commodity to the other creates co-ownership, removing ambiguity and non-liability profit.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi legal stratagem (hila) that allows partners to use commodities as capital in a shirkat al-'inan, which would otherwise be invalid. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the mechanism and the scholarly debate on whether the values must be equal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalidating factors
The text states two invalid aspects: profit on what one does not guarantee (ribh ma lam yadman) and ambiguity of capital (jahalat ra's al-mal). Understand why these make commodity partnerships invalid.
These are the 'illal (effective causes) of invalidity.
2
Understand the hila mechanism
Each partner sells half of his commodity to the other for half of the other's commodity. This creates a co-ownership (shirkat milk) where each owns half of the total goods.
The sale is mutual and immediate.
3
Analyze how the hila solves the factors
After the sale, each partner profits only from his own property (since they are co-owners), so the ribh ma lam yadman is eliminated. The capital is clearly half each, removing ambiguity.
Then they contract a partnership (shirkat 'aqd) on the co-owned goods.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on value equality
Al-Hidayah requires the values of the commodities to be equal; if not, the lesser value partner must sell only enough to equalize. Al-Tabyeen rejects this, stating that selling half of each creates 50-50 ownership regardless of value.
Al-Nihayah provides a numerical example; al-Tabyeen says it is unnecessary.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The more flexible view of al-Tabyeen is preferred by later Hanafi scholars (e.g., Ibn Nujaym), allowing the hila even with unequal values.
This affects how partners calculate profit shares after the partnership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو باع كل عرضه بنصف عرض الآخر وعقد الشركة صح) بيان للحيلة في صحة الشركة بالعروض فإن فساده بها ليس لذاتها بل للازم الباطل من أمرين : أحدهما لزوم ربح ما لم يضمن. والثاني جهالة رأس مال كل منهما عند القسمة، وكل منهما منتف في هذه الصورة فيكون كل ما يربحه الآخر ربح ما هو مضمون عليه ولا تحصل جهالة في رأس مال كل منهما عند القسمة حتى يكون ذلك بالحرز فتقع الجهالة لأنهما مستويان في المال شريكان فيه فبالضرورة يكون كل ما يحصل بينهما نصفان. وفي قوله وعقد الشركة» إشارة إلى أن بالبيع صارت شركة ملك حتى لا يجوز لكل واحد أن يتصرف في نصيب الآخر، ثم بالعقد بعده صارت شركة عقد فيجوز لكل منهما أن يتصرف في نصيب صاحبه؛ كذا في التبيين . وصرح في الهداية بأن هذا شركة ملك وفي فتح القدير إنه مشكل، ولعله فهم أن الإشارة عائدة إلى الكل وليس كذلك وإنما هي عائدة إلى البيع فقط. وأطلق في قيمة مبتاعيهما وقيده في الهداية بأن تستوي القيمتان، ولو كان بينهما تفاوت يبيع صاحب الأقل بقدر ما تثبت به الشركة. وأوضحه في النهاية بأن تكون قيمة عرض أحدهما أربعمائة وقيمة الآخر مائة فإنه يبيع صاحب الأقل أربعة أخماس عرضه بخمس عرض الآخر فيصير المتاع كله أخماساً ويكون الربح كله بينهما على قدر رأس ماليهما اهـ. ورده في التبيين بأن هذا الحمل غير محتاج إليه لأنه يجوز أن كل واحد منهما نصف ماله بنصف مال الآخر وإن تفاوتت قيمتهما يبيع حتى يصير المال بينهما نصفين وكذا العكس جائز وهو ما إذا كانت قيمتهما متساوية فباعاه على التفاوت بأن باع أحدهما ربع ماله بثلاثة أرباع مال الآخر. فعلم بذلك أن قوله «باع نصف ماله بنصف مال الآخر وقع اتفاقاً أو قصداً ليكون شاملاً للمفاوضة والعنان لأن المفاوضة شرطها التساوي بخلاف العنان. وقوله بنصف عرض الآخر» وقع اتفاقاً لأنه لو باعه بالدراهم ثم عقد الشركة في العرض الذي باعه جاز أيضاً .اهـ. وفي الذخيرة: وعلى هذا لو كان عبد بين رجلين اشتركا فيه شركة عنان أو مفاوضة جاز اهـ. وفي المحيط : رجلان لكل واحد منهما طعام فاشتركا بماليهما وخلطاهما وأحدهما أجود من الآخر فالشركة جائزة والثمن بينهما نصفان لأن هذا يشبه البيع حين خلطه على أنه بينهما. وقال في موضع آخر نص في هذا الكتاب : يقسم الثمن على قيمة الجيد وقيمة الرديء يوم باعا اهـ. هذا يقتضي أن تكون شركة ملك لا عقد.
His statement: (And if each one sells his commodity for half of the other's commodity and they contract the partnership, it is valid) - an explanation of the legal stratagem for validity of partnership with commodities. For its invalidity with them is not due to its essence but due to the necessary consequence of two invalid aspects: one is the entailment of profit on what one does not guarantee, and the second is ambiguity of each one's capital at division. And each of them is negated in this case, so everything the other profits is profit on what is guaranteed by him, and no ambiguity occurs in each one's capital at division, to the extent that there would be ambiguity, because they are equal in the property being partners in it, so necessarily everything that accrues between them is halves. In his statement 'and they contract the partnership' there is an indication that by the sale it becomes a partnership of ownership (shirkat milk) so that each is not allowed to dispose of the other's share, then by the subsequent contract it becomes a partnership of contract (shirkat 'aqd) so each is allowed to dispose of the other's share; as in al-Tabyeen. And he explicitly stated in al-Hidayah that this is a partnership of ownership, and in Fath al-Qadir it is problematic, and perhaps he understood that the reference is to the whole but it is not so; rather it is only to the sale. He left unrestricted in the value of their two purchases, but it is restricted in al-Hidayah that the two values must be equal. And if there is disparity, the owner of the lesser sells as much as establishes the partnership. It was clarified in al-Nihayah: if the value of one's commodity is 400 and the other's is 100, then the owner of the lesser sells four-fifths of his commodity for one-fifth of the other's, so the whole goods become fifths, and the profit is between them according to their capitals. This was rejected in al-Tabyeen as unnecessary, because it is permissible that each one sells half of his property for half of the other's even if their values differ, until the property becomes halves between them, and the reverse is also permissible: if their values are equal, they can sell on disparity, e.g., one sells a quarter of his property for three-quarters of the other's. So it is known that his statement 'sells half of his property for half of the other's' occurs by coincidence or intention to be inclusive of mufawadah and 'inan, because mufawadah requires equality unlike 'inan. And his statement 'for half of the other's commodity' occurs by coincidence, because if he sold it for dirhams and then contracted partnership in the sold commodity, that is also valid. In al-Dhakhirah: on this, if there is a slave between two men, they enter into partnership with it as 'inan or mufawadah, it is valid. In al-Muhit: two men each have food, they enter into partnership with their goods and mix them, one being of better quality, the partnership is valid and the price is between them half and half, because this resembles a sale when they mix it as between them. In another place in this book: the price is divided according to the value of the good quality and poor quality on the day they sold. This implies that it is a partnership of ownership not contract.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage elucidates a legal stratagem (hila) to make a partnership (shirkat al-'inan) valid when the capital consists of commodities (urud), which are not considered proper capital for shirkat al-'inan according to the Hanafi school. The invalidity arises from two factors: (1) each partner would profit from the other's property without being liable for its loss (ribh ma lam yadman), and (2) the capital of each would be ambiguous at the time of division (jahalat ra's al-mal). The stratagem is: each partner sells half of his commodity to the other for half of the other's commodity, making them co-owners of the entire mixed goods (shirkat milk). Then they contract a partnership (shirkat 'aqd) on this jointly owned pool. This solves both issues: now each is liable for the goods they own (so profit is on what is guaranteed), and the capital is clearly half each. The commentator then discusses whether the values must be equal. Al-Hidayah requires equality; if unequal, the lesser value partner must sell only enough to equalize. Al-Nihayah provides an example: one has 400, the other 100; the lesser sells 4/5 of his for 1/5 of the other's, making both own half the total. However, al-Tabyeen rejects this, arguing that even if values differ, selling half of each's property creates a 50-50 ownership regardless of value, and this is sufficient. The practical implication is that if the values are not equal, the profit shares will not correspond to the original capital contributions; but that is acceptable because after the sale, the ownership is equal. The passage also notes that if they had sold for dirhams and then partnered, it would also work. Finally, it cites al-Muhit: if they mix goods of different qualities and partnership, the price (profit) is divided half and half according to one view, or according to value according to another; the latter implies it is a partnership of ownership, not contract.

Key Terms
الحيلة (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a valid outcome that would otherwise be invalid.
ربح ما لم يضمن (ribh ma lam yadman): Profiting from something for which one does not bear the risk of loss.
جهالة رأس المال (jahalat ra's al-mal): Ambiguity in the amount of capital each partner contributed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two invalidating factors that the hila of selling half of each other's commodities solves?
A) Riba and gharar.
B) Profit on non-liability and ambiguity of capital.
C) Absence of witnesses and lack of offer.
D) Inequality of profit and loss.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hila for commodity partnership involves a reciprocal sale of half of each partner's goods to create co-ownership, eliminating the prohibitions of profit on non-liability and capital ambiguity.

Shirkah — Partnership

The Hanafi Definition of Shirkat al-'Inan: Agency Only
Defines shirkat al-'inan as a partnership based solely on agency, not suretyship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shirkat al-'inan and explain why it excludes kafalah.

Core Idea
Shirkat al-'inan is a pure agency partnership — suretyship has no place in its contract.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the definition of shirkat al-'inan given in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It emphasizes that the partnership is based solely on agency (wakalah), not on suretyship (kafalah). The etymology of 'inan supports this restriction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining phrase
The author says 'وعنان أن تضمنت وكالة فقط' — 'And 'inan is if it includes agency only.' This is the core definition.
The word 'only' (فقط) is key.
2
Understand the etymology of 'inan'
The Qamus cites three possible meanings: being in something specific, one party approaching the other, or equality (like the strands of a bridle). None imply suretyship.
Etymology supports agency-only interpretation.
3
Explain why kafalah is excluded
The word 'inan is derived from 'i'tirad (opposition), not kafalah. Therefore, a contract named 'inan cannot include suretyship because the ruling must match the implication of the word.
Hanafis strictly follow linguistic implications.
4
Note the condition from al-Bazzaziyyah
The presence of capital is not required at the time of contract; it is required at the time of purchase. This is a separate condition that does not affect the definition.
This distinguishes form from substance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وعنان أن تضمنت وكالة فقط) بالرفع عطف على مفاوضة بيان للنوع الثاني من شركة العقد. وفي القاموس إنها على وزن كتاب في الشركة أن يكون في شيء خاص دون سائر مالهما أو هو أن يعارض رجلاً بالشراء فيقول اشركني معك أو هو أن يكونا سواء في الشركة لأن عنان الدابة طاقتان متساويتان .اهـ. وإنما انعقدت على الوكالة لتحقيق مقصوده كما بينا. ومعنى قوله «فقط» أنها لا تنعقد على الكفالة لأن اللفظ مشتق من الاعتراض يقال عن له أي اعترض، وهذا لا ينبئ عن الكفالة وحكم التصرف لا يثبت بخلاف مقتضى اللفظ فظاهر كلامه أنهما لو عقداها على الكفالة لا تكون عناناً لكنه مقيد بما إذا كانت باقي شروط البزازية فإنه قال : ولم يشترط حضور المال وقت العقد وهو صحيح، بل الشرط وجوده وقت الشراء، ثم ذكر مسألة ما لو دفع إلى رجل ألفاً وقال أخرج مثلها .
His statement: (And 'inan is if it includes agency only) - with nominative case as an appositive to mufawadah, an explanation of the second type of partnership by contract. In al-Qamus: it is on the pattern of kitab in partnership that it is in something specific without the rest of their property, or that one party approaches the other for purchase saying 'partner me with you', or that they are equal in the partnership because the 'inan of an animal is two equal strands. It is concluded on agency to achieve its purpose as we explained. The meaning of his word 'only' is that it is not concluded on suretyship because the word is derived from 'i'tirad (opposition); it is said 'ana lahu' i.e. he opposed, and this does not indicate suretyship, and the ruling of disposition is not established contrary to the implication of the word. So the apparent meaning of his speech is that if they contract it on suretyship, it is not 'inan, but it is restricted by the remaining conditions of al-Bazzaziyyah, for he said: He did not stipulate the presence of money at the time of contract, and that is correct; rather the condition is its existence at the time of purchase. Then he mentioned the issue of one who gives a man a thousand and says 'bring out the like of it'.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the second type of partnership by contract (shirkat al-'aqd), namely shirkat al-'inan. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines it as a partnership that includes agency (wakalah) only, excluding kafalah (suretyship). The commentator cites the Qamus: the term 'inan is derived from the notion of being in something specific (not general) or from the idea of equality (like the two strands of a horse's bridle). The partnership is concluded on the basis of agency (each partner is an agent for the other) because that achieves the purpose of buying and selling. The word 'only' (faqat) indicates that kafalah is not included, as the word 'inan etymologically implies opposition or equality, not suretyship. Therefore, if the partners contract on the basis of kafalah, it would not be a valid 'inan contract. However, the commentator adds a restriction from al-Bazzaziyyah: the condition of presence of capital at the time of contract is not required; rather it is required at the time of purchase. This aligns with the earlier lesson on capital presence.

Key Terms
شركة العنان (shirkat al-'inan): A partnership where each partner is an agent for the other in a specific venture, without suretyship.
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; each partner acts as an agent for the other in purchase/sale.
كفالة (kafalah): Suretyship; guarantee of another's liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition of shirkat al-'inan, what is excluded from the contract?
A) Agency (wakalah).
B) Suretyship (kafalah).
C) Profit-sharing.
D) Loss-sharing.

Key Takeaway
Shirkat al-'inan is a partnership of pure agency; any inclusion of suretyship takes it out of the 'inan category.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate

Partnership Valid with Unequal Profit Despite Equal Capital
Establishing the validity of partnership with unequal profit shares and responding to dissenting views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partnership with unequal profit shares, cite the hadith proof, and explain the response to Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Profit in partnership is determined by agreement, not forced proportionality to capital.

Partnership (shirkah) is a cornerstone of Islamic commercial law. A common question arises: if partners contribute equal capital, must profit shares be equal? The Hanafi school, relying on a clear hadith and practical necessity, allows any profit split by mutual consent. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the opposing view, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling: a partnership is valid (sahih) even with unequal profit shares despite equal capital, or vice versa.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Recognize the opposing view
Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and al-Shafi'i hold that such disparity is invalid; profit must follow capital proportion.
Their reasoning: profit is like the growth of jointly owned property, proportional to ownership.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Profit is according to their condition, and loss is according to the two capitals.' The phrase 'according to their condition' is general, allowing any agreed split.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala) in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to opponents
Profit is earned not only by capital but also by work, as in mudarabah. Hence a partner may deserve more due to skill or effort. The hadith does not differentiate, and practical necessity demands flexibility.
The Hanafi school also uses qiyas to mudarabah to justify disparity.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, the partnership is valid and the agreed profit share is enforceable. Under Zufar/Shafi'i, the contract would be invalid unless profits are proportionate.
The mufta bihi is the majority Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتصح مع التساوي في المال دون الربح وعكسه وهو التفاضل في المال والتساوي في الربح. وقال زفر والشافعي : لا يجوز لأن التفاضل فيه يؤدي إلى ربح يضمن فإن المال إذا كان نصفين والربح أثلاثاً فصاحب الزيادة يستحقها بلا ضمان إذ الضمان بقدر المال لأن الشركة عندهما في الربح كالشركة في الأصل ولهذا يشترطان الخلط المال بمنزلة نماء الأعيان فيستحق بقدر الملك في الأصل ولنا قوله عليه السلام ربح «الربح على ما شرطا والوضيعة على قدر المالين» ولم يفصل ولأن الربح كما يستحق بالمال يستحق بالعمل كما في المضاربة، وقد يكون أحدهما أحذق وأهدى أو أكثر عملاً فلا يرضى بالمساواة فمست الحاجة إلى التفاضل
His saying: (And it is valid with equality in capital without profit and its opposite, which is disparity in capital and equality in profit. And Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible because disparity in it leads to profit that is guaranteed [without liability]? For if capital is half and profit is thirds, the one with increase deserves it without guarantee since guarantee is according to capital because partnership in profit with them is like partnership in the original, and for this they require mixing of capital as a substitute for growth of assets, so it is deserved according to ownership in the original. And we have his saying, peace be upon him: 'Profit is according to what they condition, and loss is according to the two capitals.' And he did not differentiate, and because profit is deserved by capital and also by work as in mudarabah, and one of them may be more skilled or more knowledgeable or do more work, so he is not satisfied with equality, so there is need for disparity.)
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (with Zufar) and also an inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i. The author is commenting on the matn's ruling that a partnership is valid when the partners have equal capital but unequal profit shares, or vice versa (unequal capital but equal profit). Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that such disparity is invalid because, in their view, profit in a partnership is analogous to the growth of owned assets: just as the yield of jointly owned property is distributed according to ownership shares, so profit should be proportional to capital. They thus require mixing of capitals and view profit as earned solely by capital. The Hanafi response, attributed to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, relies on the hadith 'Profit is according to their condition, and loss is according to the capitals' which does not differentiate between equal and unequal profit shares. Additionally, they argue that profit can also be earned through work, as in a mudarabah contract. Therefore, one partner may deserve more profit due to greater skill or effort, and the necessity of commercial practice requires allowing such flexibility. The dispute thus hinges on whether profit is seen purely as a return on capital or also as compensation for labour.

Key Terms
شركة (shirkah): A contractual partnership between two or more persons for joint investment and profit.
عنان (‘inān): A type of partnership where partners contribute capital and work, but each is not a guarantor of the other unless stipulated.
ربح (ribḥ): Profit generated by the partnership business.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a partnership where two partners contribute equal capital but agree that one partner receives 70% of the profit?
A) Valid, because profit is according to their condition.
B) Invalid, because profit must be proportional to capital.
C) Valid only if they also mix their capitals.
D) Invalid because it leads to uncertainty (gharar).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, partnership profit shares are based on mutual agreement, not forced proportionality, allowing flexibility for work and skill.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
8 min
Condition that Greater Profit Goes to More Active Partner
Explaining the qualification that extra profit should be for the working partner and the three cases of work distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the later Hanafi condition for valid unequal profit shares in an 'inan partnership and apply it to different work scenarios.

Core Idea
Unequal profit shares are valid only when the larger share goes to the partner who works more.

In this passage, the author expands on the permissibility of unequal profit shares in an 'inan partnership. While earlier authorities allowed absolute disparity, later Hanafi scholars restricted it to cases where the larger profit corresponds to greater work contribution. We will explore the reasoning behind this qualification and examine three work-distribution scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Recognize that stipulating all profit for one partner is invalid because it changes the contract to a loan or bailment.
2
Understand the resemblance arguments
The partnership resembles mudarabah (profit without liability) and partnership (work can be required). This combined reasoning allows flexibility.
These resemblances justify the permissibility of unequal profit shares when work is aligned.
3
Locate the qualification from later authorities
Al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir restrict the absolute permissibility to cases where the larger profit share is for the partner who works more or contributes more labour.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Examine the three cases from al-Muhit
The three scenarios are: (1) both work, profit half-half; (2) one works, profit as stipulated; (3) condition of work on one, valid if aligned with profit share.
Illness does not deprive a partner of his share.
5
Apply the ruling to determine validity
Given a scenario, check if the larger profit share is given to the partner who does more work. If not, the condition is invalid and profit is distributed according to capital ratio.
Remember: the later view prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيد بالشركة في الربح لأن اشتراط الربح كله لأحدهما غير صحيح لأنه يخرج العقد به من الشركة ومن المضاربة أيضاً إلى قرض باشتراطه للعامل أو إلى بضاعة باشتراطه لرب المال وهذا العقد يشبه المضاربة من حيث إنه يعمل في مال الشريك، ويشبه الشركة اسماً وعملاً فإنهما يعملان معاً فعملنا بشبه المضاربة، وقلنا يصح اشتراط الربح من غير ضمان وبشبه الشركة حتى لا تبطل باشتراط العمل عليهما. وقد أطلق المصنف تبعاً للهداية جواز التفاضل في الربح مع التساوي في المال، وقيده في التبيين وفتح القدير بأن يشترطا الأكثر للعامل منهما أو لأكثرهما عملاً، أما إن شرطاه للقاعد أو لأقلهما عملاً فلا يجوز، ولم يشترط المصنف لاستحقاق الربح المشروط اجتماعهما على العمل لأنه غير شرط لتضمنها الوكالة ولذا قال في البزازية : اشتركا وعمل أحدهما في غيبة الآخر فلما حضر أعطاه حصته ثم غاب الآخر وعمل الآخر فلما حضر الغائب أبى أن يعطيه حصته من الربح، إن كان الشرط أن يعملا جميعاً وشتى فما كان من تجارتهما من الربح فبينهما على الشرط عملاً أو عمل أحدهما، فإن مرض أحدهما ولم يعمل وعمل الآخر فهو بينهما. وفي المحيط ثم المسألة على ثلاثة أوجه الأول أن يشترطا العمل عليهما والربح بينهما نصفين والوضيعة على قدر رأس المال، فإن عمل أحدهما دون الآخر فالربح بينهما على ما شرطا، وإن شرطا العمل على أحدهما ينظر؛ إن شرطا العمل على أكثرهما ربحاً جاز، وإن شرطاه على بتمام معناها كما مر، ولا يخفى أن فيه التصريح بالكفالة فقد ثبتت الكفالة فيه مع التصريح بها ولم تجعل قصداً بل ضمناً قوله: (أما إن شرطاه للقاعد الخ) لم يذكر ما لو اشترطاه للقاعد وكان ماله أكثر كما لو وضع القاعدة تسعة آلاف مثلاً ووضع العامل ألفاً واشترطا ثلثي الربح للقاعد والثلث للعامل وهذه تقع كثيراً. ويؤخذ عدم الجواز من قول المحيط الآتي قريباً «وإن شرطا العمل على أقلهما ربحاً خاصة لا يجوز والربح بينهما على قدر رأس مالهما فإنه يفيد أنه إذا اختلف رأس المال وكان العامل هو الأقل ربحاً لا يجوز الشرط بل يكون الربح على قدر المال، وحينئذ فيحصل على العامل إجحاف زائد لأنه يحصل له في صورتنا المذكورة عشر الربح مع تعبه في العمل لكن ما ننقله عن الظهيرية فيه ما يفيد الجواز فتأمله قوله: (وفي المحيط ثم المسألة على ثلاثة أوجه الخ) ذكر ذلك في الظهيرية ثم قال بعده: بيان ما ذكرنا فيما ذكر محمد في الأصل إذا جاء أحدهما بألف درهم والآخر بألفين واشتركا على أن الربح بينهما نصفان والعمل عليهما فهو جائز ويصير صاحب الألف في معنى المضارب إلا أن معنى المضاربة تبع لمعنى الشركة والعبرة للأصل دون التبع فلا يضرهما
Restricted by partnership in profit because stipulating all profit for one is invalid as it changes the contract from partnership and mudarabah to a loan (if for the worker) or to a bailment (if for the capital owner). This contract resembles mudarabah in that one works in the other's capital, and resembles partnership in name and work. So we act on the resemblance to mudarabah and say it is valid to stipulate profit without liability, and on resemblance to partnership so that it is not invalidated by stipulating work on both. The author, following al-Hidayah, absolutely permitted disparity in profit with equality in capital, but in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir it is restricted to stipulating the larger share for the worker of the two or the one who does more work. If they stipulate it for the idle or the one who does less work, it is not valid. The author did not require for entitlement to the stipulated profit that both work together because it is not a condition, as it includes agency. Hence, in al-Bazzaziyya: They formed a partnership and one worked in the absence of the other; when he returned, he gave him his share. Then the other left and the first worked; when the absentee returned, he refused to give him his share of the profit. If the condition was that both work together, then whatever profit came from their trade is between them according to the condition, whether one worked or the other. If one fell ill and did not work while the other worked, the profit is between them. In al-Muhit: The issue has three aspects. First, they stipulate work on both and profit between them half and half, and loss according to capital. If one works without the other, profit is between them as stipulated. If they stipulate work on one, it is considered: if they stipulate work on the one with higher profit share, it is valid; if they stipulate it...
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the qualification of the previous ruling. The author begins by stating that stipulating all profit for one partner is invalid because it transforms the contract from partnership into either a loan (if the profit goes to the worker) or a bailment (if it goes to the capital owner). The contract resembles both mudarabah and partnership, and Hanafi jurisprudence uses a combined reasoning: from mudarabah, profit can be stipulated without liability; from partnership, work can be required of both without invalidity. The author then notes that while al-Hidayah and the matn categorically permit unequal profit shares with equal capital, later works like al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir restrict this permissibility to cases where the larger profit share is given to the partner who works more or performs more labour. If the larger share is given to the idle partner or the one who works less, it is not valid. The author then cites al-Bazzaziyya with an example: if partners agree that both should work, but one works in the absence of the other, the profit is shared as stipulated; illness of one does not deprive him of his share. Finally, al-Muhit is quoted presenting three cases regarding work and profit distribution, emphasizing that the condition of work must be aligned with profit shares; otherwise, the profit reverts to the capital ratio. The passage also touches on kafalah (guarantee) in 'inan partnership, stating that stipulating kafalah does not change the nature of the contract. The author ends with a discussion of a specific scenario where the idle partner has more capital but takes a larger profit share, citing al-Zahiriyya to indicate a possible difference of opinion.

Key Terms
عمل (‘amal): Work or labour contributed by a partner to the partnership business.
قاعد (qā‘id): A partner who does not work or is idle; the one not actively participating in the business.
كفالة (kafālah): Guarantee or surety; in 'inan partnership, it is not implicit but can be explicitly stipulated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi 'inan partnership, what condition must be met for stipulating unequal profit shares with equal capital?
A) The larger share must go to the partner who works more.
B) The partners must mix their capitals.
C) The partnership must be for a fixed term.
D) The profit shares must be equal.

Key Takeaway
In a Hanafi 'inan partnership, unequal profit shares with equal capital are valid only if the larger share is given to the partner who contributes more work.

Shirkah — Partnership

Permissibility of Differential Profit Sharing in Partnership
Explaining the ruling on differential profit with proof and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on differential profit sharing, identify the hadith proof, and apply the condition that the larger share must be for the more active partner.

Core Idea
Profit can be divided by stipulation, not by capital ratio; but the larger share must be for the more active partner.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key issue in partnership (shirkah): can partners agree to unequal profit shares even if their capital contributions are equal? The Hanafi school, based on a hadith and reasoning by analogy to mudarabah, permits this with a crucial condition that the larger share goes to the partner who works more or is more skilled. We will examine the proof, the intra-school disagreement, and the practical restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the core question is whether profit shares can be stipulated independently of capital ratios. The passage addresses the validity of differential profit shares in a partnership where both contribute capital and work.
2
State the Hanafi position and primary proof
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that profit may be divided by stipulation, even if capital is equal. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Profit is according to what they stipulate, and loss is according to the two capitals.' This hadith does not tie profit to capital proportion.
The hadith is zanni in thubut and dalala, but it is the main textual evidence.
3
Distinguish the Sahibayn's opposing view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that profit must be proportional to capital when capitals are equal, because they analogize profit to growth of physical assets that belong proportionally to owners.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the later restriction (taqyid)
Later Hanafi commentators like al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir restricted the absolute permission: the larger share must be for the partner who works more or is more skilled. If the larger share is stipulated for the idle partner, the condition is invalid and profit reverts to the default proportional distribution.
This restriction is mufta bihi.
5
Work through scenarios from al-Muhit
Analyze the practical scenarios: both work, one works while other is idle, or stipulating work on one partner. Understand how the ruling applies in each case, especially the case where capital differs and the worker gets less profit.
The author also notes a conflicting narration from al-Zahiriyyah, so encourage pondering.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشركة فصار . بقدر رأس المال لأن الشركة عندهما في الربح كالشركة في الأصل ولهذا يشترطان الخلط المال بمنزلة نماء الأعيان فيستحق بقدر الملك في الأصل ولنا قوله عليه السلام ربح «الربح على ما شرطا والوضيعة على قدر المالين ولم يفصل ولأن الربح كما يستحق بالمال يستحق بالعمل كما في المضاربة، وقد يكون أحدهما أحذق وأهدى أو أكثر عملاً فلا يرضى بالمساواة فمست الحاجة إلى التفاضل قيد بالشركة في الربح لأن اشتراط الربح كله لأحدهما غير صحيح لأنه يخرج العقد به من الشركة ومن المضاربة أيضاً إلى قرض باشتراطه للعامل أو إلى بضاعة باشتراطه لرب المال وهذا العقد يشبه المضاربة من حيث إنه يعمل في مال الشريك، ويشبه التساوي في المال، وقيده في التبيين وفتح القدير بأن يشترطا الأكثر للعامل منهما أو لأكثرهما عملاً، أما إن شرطاه للقاعد أو لأقلهما عملاً فلا يجوز، ولم يشترط المصنف لاستحقاق الربح المشروط اجتماعهما على العمل لأنه غير شرط لتضمنها الوكالة ولذا قال في البزازية : اشتركا وعمل أحدهما في غيبة الآخر فلما حضر أعطاه حصته ثم غاب الآخر وعمل الآخر فلما حضر الغائب أبى أن يعطيه حصته من الربح، إن كان الشرط أن يعملا جميعاً وشتى فما كان من تجارتهما من الربح فبينهما على الشرط عملاً أو عمل أحدهما، فإن مرض أحدهما ولم يعمل وعمل الآخر فهو بينهما. وفي المحيط ثم المسألة على ثلاثة أوجه الأول أن يشترطا العمل عليهما والربح بينهما نصفين والوضيعة على قدر رأس المال، فإن عمل أحدهما دون الآخر فالربح بينهما على ما شرطا، وإن شرطا العمل على أحدهما ينظر ؛ إن شرطا العمل على أكثرهما ربحاً جاز، وإن شرطاه على بتمام معناها كما مر ، ولا يخفى أن فيه التصريح بالكفالة فقد ثبتت الكفالة فيه مع التصريح بها ولم تجعل قصداً بل ضمناً قوله : (أما إن شرطاه للقاعد (الخ) لم يذكر ما لو اشترطاه للقاعد وكان ماله أكثر كما لو وضع القاعدة تسعة آلاف مثلاً ووضع العامل ألفاً واشترطا ثلثي الربح للقاعد والثلث للعامل وهذه تقع كثيراً. ويؤخذ عدم الجواز من قول المحيط الآتي قريباً «وإن شرطا العمل على أقلهما ربحاً خاصة لا يجوز والربح بينهما على قدر رأس مالهما فإنه يفيد أنه إذا اختلف رأس المال وكان العامل هو الأقل ربحاً لا يجوز الشرط بل يكون الربح على قدر المال، وحينئذ فيحصل على العامل إجحاف زائد لأنه يحصل له في صورتنا المذكورة عشر الربح مع تعبه في العمل لكن ما ننقله عن الظهيرية فيه ما يفيد الجواز فتأمله قوله : (وفي المحيط ثم المسألة على ثلاثة أوجه الخ) ذكر ذلك في الظهيرية ثم قال بعده : بيان ما ذكرنا فيما ذكر محمد في الأصل إذا جاء أحدهما بألف درهم والآخر بألفين واشتركا على أن الربح بينهما نصفان والعمل عليهما فهو جائز ويصير صاحب الألف في معنى المضارب إلا أن معنى المضاربة تبع لمعنى الشركة والعبرة للأصل دون التبع فلا يضرهما
The Book of Partnership. Then it became... according to the extent of capital, because according to them (the two companions) the partnership in profit is like partnership in the principal, and therefore they stipulate mixing; wealth is like the growth of assets, so it is entitled according to ownership in the principal. And our proof is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Profit is according to what they stipulate, and loss is according to the two capitals.' And he did not differentiate. And because profit, as it is earned by capital, is also earned by work, as in mudarabah. And one of them may be more skilled, more experienced, or work more, so he is not satisfied with equality, thus there is a need for differentiation. It is restricted to partnership in profit because stipulating all profit for one of them is invalid, as it takes the contract out of partnership and also out of mudarabah into a loan if stipulated for the worker, or into a sleeping partnership if stipulated for the capital owner. This contract resembles mudarabah in that one works in the partner's wealth, and resembles partnership in name and work because both work together. So we acted upon the resemblance to mudarabah and said the stipulation of profit without guarantee is valid, and upon the resemblance to partnership so that it is not invalidated by stipulating work on both. The author, following al-Hidayah, has absolutely allowed differentiation in profit with equality in capital, but it is restricted in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir to stipulating the larger share for the worker or the one who works more. As for if they stipulate it for the idle or the one who works less, it is not permissible. The author did not stipulate for entitlement to the stipulated profit that both engage in work, because it is not a condition for the contract includes agency. Hence it is said in al-Bazzaziyyah: If they contracted and one worked in the absence of the other, then when he came he gave him his share, then the other went away and the other worked, then when the absent one came back he refused to give him his share of profit. If the condition was that both work together, then whatever profit came from their trade is between them according to the condition, whether they worked or one worked. If one of them fell ill and did not work and the other worked, it is between them. In al-Muhit: The issue is of three types: First, that they stipulate work on both, profit half and loss according to capital; if one works without the other, profit is between them as stipulated; if they stipulate work on one, then look: if they stipulate work on the one with more profit, it is valid; if they stipulate it on the one with less profit specifically, it is not valid, and profit is between them according to capital. End quote. And there is no harm in the clarity that it contains express mention of guarantee; the guarantee is established in it with express mention and not made an intent but implied. His word: 'As for if they stipulate it for the idle...' he did not mention the case where they stipulate for the idle and his capital is more, like if the idle one puts nine thousand and the worker puts one thousand and they stipulate two thirds of profit for the idle and one third for the worker, and this occurs often. One infers the non-permissibility from the saying of al-Muhit below: 'And if they stipulate work on the one with less profit specifically, it is not valid, and profit is between them according to their capitals.' For it indicates that if capital differs and the worker is the one with less profit, the condition is not valid, rather profit is according to capital. Then the worker would suffer excessive injustice because he would get in our mentioned example one tenth of the profit with his effort in work. But what we transmit from al-Zahiriyyah contains something indicating permissibility, so ponder. His word: 'And in al-Muhit: Then the issue is of three types...' He mentioned that in al-Zahiriyyah then said after it: Elaboration of what we mentioned: Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl: If one of them brings one thousand dirhams and the other two thousand, and they contract on profit half and loss according to capital, it is valid, and the owner of one thousand becomes in the sense of a mudarib, except that the meaning of mudarabah is subordinate to the meaning of partnership, and consideration is to the original not the subordinate, so it does not harm them.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on profit sharing in partnership (shirkah). The author begins by stating the position of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that profit must be proportional to capital because they analogize profit to the growth of physical assets. The author then presents the Hanafi proof: the hadith 'Profit is according to their stipulation, and loss is according to the two capitals' which does not differentiate between equal and unequal capital. Rational arguments follow: profit is also earned by work, so a more skilled partner may deserve more. The author clarifies that the absolute permission of differential profit is restricted by later scholars (al-Tabyin, Fath al-Qadir) to cases where the larger share is stipulated for the more working partner; if stipulated for the idle partner, it is invalid. The passage then discusses scenarios from al-Muhit: (1) both work, (2) one works without the other, (3) stipulating work on one partner. The author also engages with a practical case where the idle partner has more capital and the worker less, showing that normally it would be invalid, but a report from al-Zahiriyyah suggests permissibility. The lesson demonstrates the interplay between textual proof (hadith), rational analogy (qiyas), and later scholarly refinement (taqyid).

Key Terms
الربح (al-ribh): Profit generated from the partnership trade, distributed according to stipulation.
الوضيعة (al-wadi'ah): Loss suffered in the partnership, distributed in proportion to capital contribution.
التفاضل (al-tafadul): Difference or inequality in shares (e.g., profit shares) between partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi view, which of the following profit-sharing conditions is permissible?
A) Both contribute equal capital, profit split 50-50, one works and one is idle.
B) Both contribute equal capital, profit split 70-30 in favor of the partner who works more.
C) Both contribute equal capital, profit split 70-30 in favor of the idle partner.
D) One contributes all capital, profit split 80-20 in favor of the capital owner, worker gets 20%.

Key Takeaway
Profit sharing in Hanafi partnership can be unequal by mutual agreement, but the larger share must be given to the partner who works more or is more skilled.

Partnership: Partial Capital and Different Currencies
Expanding two rulings on partnership capital from Kanz al-Daqa'iq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that in the Hanafi school, partnership is valid with part of wealth and with different types of capital, and identify the reasoning based on the text.

Core Idea
Partnership is valid with part of wealth and with different currencies; equality and same type are not conditions.

The Hanafi school takes a flexible approach to partnership capital. In this passage, the commentator clarifies two key rulings from the matn: first, partners may invest only a portion of their wealth, and second, the capitals can be of different types (e.g., gold and silver). Understanding these rulings removes common misconceptions about what makes a partnership contract valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two distinct rulings about capital: (1) partnership is valid with part of wealth, (2) partnership is valid with different types of capital.
The text says 'وبعض المال' and 'وبخلاف الجنس'.
2
Understand the legal basis for each
For partial capital: equality is not a condition because the wording does not require it. For different types: mixing is not a condition according to the Hanafi school.
The reasons are explicitly given in the commentary.
3
Extend the second ruling to different qualities
The text states that it is valid a fortiori (بالأولى) when capitals are of the same type but different quality, such as black and white dirhams, even if their values differ.
This shows the principle of priority.
4
Note the profit rule
Profit is according to what the parties stipulate, regardless of capital composition.
This is consistent with Hanafi partnership rules.
5
Connect to broader Hanafi principles
The rulings reflect Hanafi leniency in partnership conditions, prioritizing ease of transaction over strict formalism.
Compare with other schools that require same type and full investment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبعض المال) يعني يصح أن يعقدها كل واحد منهما ببعض ماله دون البعض لأن المساواة في المال ليس بشرط إذ اللفظ لا يقتضيه، وقدمنا ما تصح به الشركة من الأموال مفاوضة أو عناناً قوله : (وبخلاف (الجنس) بأن يكون من أحدهما دنانير ومن الآخر دراهم لعدم اشتراط الخلط عندنا فجازت في متحد الجنس ومختلفه، وتجوز مع اختلاف الوصف فقط بالأولى كما إذا كان من أحدهما دراهم سود ومن الآخر دراهم بيض وإن تفاوتت قيمتها والربح على ما شرطا
His saying: 'And with part of the wealth' means it is valid for each of them to contract with part of his wealth, not all of it, because equality in capital is not a condition since the wording does not require it. And we have already presented what types of wealth partnership is valid with, whether mufawadah or 'inan. His saying: 'And with difference of type' such that one has dinars and the other dirhams, because mixing is not a condition according to us, so it is valid with same type and different types. And it is valid with difference in description only, a fortiori, as when one has black dirhams and the other white dirhams, even if their values differ, and profit is according to their stipulation.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage explains two rulings from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. First, partnership (shirkah) is valid even if each partner invests only part of their total wealth; equality of capital amounts is not required. Second, partnership is valid even if the capitals are of different types (e.g., gold dinars vs. silver dirhams) because mixing is not a condition in the Hanafi school. This also applies a fortiori if they are the same type but different quality (e.g., black vs. white dirhams). Profit sharing follows their stipulation regardless.

Key Terms
مفاوضة (mufawadah): A type of full partnership where both partners are equal in capital, profit, and liability.
عنان ('inan): A limited partnership where partners may have unequal capital and profit shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is a partnership valid if one partner contributes gold dinars and the other silver dirhams?
A) No, because type must be the same
B) Yes, because mixing is not a condition
C) Yes, but only if they are of equal value
D) No, because the contract would be ambiguous

Key Takeaway
Partnership capital in the Hanafi school is flexible: it need not be all wealth and can be of different types or currencies, with profit shares as agreed.

Shirkah — Partnership

Mixing of Capitals Not Required in Partnership
Explaining that physical mixing of capital is not a condition for partnership validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that physical mixing of capital is not required for partnership validity and explain the rational arguments (dalil aqli) supporting it.

Core Idea
Partnership is based on contract, not capital — mixing of coins is irrelevant because profit arises from trade, not the coins themselves.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that mixing (khalṭ) of capital is not a condition for a valid partnership (shirkah) in the Hanafi school. The author presents two rational arguments: the contract itself creates the partnership in profit, and since dirhams and dinars are fungible, profit comes from transaction, not the capital. This ruling clarifies a common misconception and shows the Hanafi focus on contractual intention over physical form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the condition at issue
The passage states that lack of mixing does not invalidate the partnership. Identify that mixing is not a condition (shart) for validity.
The negation of a condition is asserted: 'wa-'adam al-khalṭ' meaning it is valid without mixing.
2
Examine the first rational argument (dalil aqli)
Partnership in profit is based on the contract, not the capital. The contract itself creates the legal relationship of profit-sharing, so physical mixing is unnecessary.
The text says: 'li-anna al-shirkah fī al-ribḥ mustanidah ilā al-'aqd dūna al-māl'.
3
Examine the second rational argument
Dirhams and dinars are not specific (ghayr muta'ayyin), so profit is derived from the transaction (taṣarruf), not from the capital itself. Each partner is both a principal (asīl) in his share and an agent (wakīl) in his partner's share.
Because coins are fungible, the ownership of profit does not depend on physical identification of capital.
4
Understand the analogy to mudarabah
The text says it becomes like mudarabah (qirad), where one party provides capital and the other labor. In mudarabah, mixing is not required, so similarly in shirkah.
Analogy (qiyas) to mudarabah reinforces that mixing is not a condition.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider two partners who contribute capital but do not physically mix it. Per the Hanafi ruling, the partnership is valid because the contract and the trade activity create the profit-sharing.
This ruling facilitates business by not imposing a physical condition that may be impractical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وعدم الخلط أي تصح وإن لم يخلطا المالين لأن الشركة في الربح مستندة إلى العقد دون المال لأن العقد يسمى شركة ولا بد من تحقيق معنى هذا الاسم فيه فلم يكن الخلط شرطاً، ولأن الدراهم والدنانير لا يتعينان فلا يستفاد الربح برأس المال وإنما يستفاد بالتصرف لأنه في النصف أصيل وفي النصف وكيل، وإذا تحققت الشركة في التصرف بدون الخلط تحققت في المستفاد به وهو الربح بدونه وصارت كالمضاربة

For the contract is called partnership, and it is necessary to realize the meaning of this name in it, so mixing was not a condition. And because dirhams and dinars are not specific, so profit is not derived from the capital itself but rather from the transaction, for each is a principal in half and an agent in half. When partnership in the transaction is realized without mixing, it is realized in what is gained thereby, which is profit, without mixing, and it becomes like mudarabah.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage addresses the condition of mixing (khalṭ) the capital in partnership. The Hanafi school holds that mixing is not a condition because the partnership contract itself creates the legal relationship of sharing profit, not the physical mixing of coins. Since dirhams and dinars are not specific entities (ghayr muta'ayyin), profit comes from trade activity, not from the capital itself. Each partner is both a principal (asīl) in his share and an agent (wakīl) in his partner's share. Therefore, mixing is not required, and the arrangement resembles mudarabah (where one provides capital and the other work).

Key Terms
الخلط (al-khalṭ): Physical mixing of the capital goods (coins) so that they become indistinguishable.
مضاربة (mudarabah): A silent partnership where one provides capital and the other labor, profit shared by agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because mixing is impossible with coins
C) Because the Quran exempts mixing
D) Because partners always have separate funds

Key Takeaway
Physical mixing of capital is not a condition for partnership validity because the contract itself creates the profit-sharing relationship, and profit is derived from trade, not from the capital itself.

Liability in Partnership: Only Contracting Partner is Sued
Expansion of a base ruling on partner liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why, in a Hanafi partnership, only the partner who contracts a sale is directly liable to the buyer, and distinguish between wakalah and kafalah in this context.

Core Idea
Partnership implies agency, not guarantee—so only the contracting partner bears direct liability.

When two partners run a business, one may buy goods on credit. If the seller demands payment, whom can he sue? The Hanafi rule is clear: only the partner who made the purchase. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind that rule, focusing on the nature of partnership as mutual agency (wakālah) without mutual guarantee (kafālah). Understanding this distinction is key to grasping partner liability in Hanafi commercial law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the operative rule: the seller can demand the price only from the partner who contracted the sale, not from the other partner.
The phrase 'وطولب المشتري بالثمن فقط' is the core ruling.
2
Understand the legal basis: wakālah vs. kafālah
The commentator explains that partnership inherently includes agency (wakālah) for each partner to act on behalf of the other, but does not include guarantee (kafālah). This is why the non-contracting partner is not directly liable.
Agency makes the contract valid for the partnership; guarantee would create joint liability.
3
Apply to the scenario
In a sale by one partner, the contracting partner is the direct obligor (aṣīl) for the price. The other partner is not a guarantor, so the seller's recourse is limited.
This rule applies whether the partnership is ʿinān or mudārabah, unless kafālah is explicitly stipulated.
4
Contrast with possible misconceptions
Some might think all partners are jointly liable for partnership debts. This ruling clarifies that joint liability is not automatic; it requires explicit guarantee.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وطولب المشتري بالثمن فقط) أي دون صاحبه لما بينا أنها تتضمن الوكالة دون الكفالة والوكيل الأصيل هو في الحقوق
His saying: 'And the buyer only demands the price from the one partner' meaning not from his partner, because we have explained that partnership includes agency, not guarantee, and the agent is a principal in rights.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This ruling explains that when a partnership buys goods on credit, the seller can only demand the price from the partner who actually made the purchase contract. The other partner is not directly liable because partnership implies mutual agency (wakālah) but not mutual guarantee (kafālah). Each partner is considered a principal (aṣīl) in his own right for the contract he performs, not a guarantor for his co-partner. Therefore, the buyer's recourse is limited to the contracting partner.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakālah): Agency: each partner acts as agent for the other in trade transactions.
كفالة (kafālah): Guarantee: liability for another's debt.
أصيل (aṣīl): Principal: the partner who contracts is considered the principal for that transaction, bearing direct rights and obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the non-contracting partner was not present at the sale.
B) Because partnership includes agency but not guarantee.
C) Because the non-contracting partner has no capital.
D) Because the sale is void if both partners are not parties.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi partnership, the seller can only sue the partner who made the contract because partnership implies agency (wakālah) without guarantee (kafālah).
