Legal Device to Make Capital Guaranteed in Mudarabah
Describes a legal stratagem from al-Zayla'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the steps of the ḥīlah described by al-Zayla'i and explain how it transforms the mudarib from trustee to debtor.

Core Idea
A loan followed by a mudarabah contract makes the worker liable for capital loss.

In a standard mudarabah, the mudarib is a trustee (amīn) and is not liable for loss of capital. This creates risk for the capital owner. To address this, Hanafi jurists devised a legal stratagem (ḥīlah) that uses a preliminary loan contract to make the capital guaranteed. Al-Zayla'i explains the mechanism clearly, showing the interplay of contracts to achieve a permissible outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
In standard mudarabah, the mudarib is not liable for capital loss. Recognize why an investor might want to make the capital guaranteed.
The worker is a trustee, not a debtor.
2
Structure the ḥīlah – Loan first
The capital owner gives the entire capital as a loan (qarḍ) to the would-be worker, making him a debtor. Witnesses are required.
A loan creates a debt obligation; the borrower is liable for repayment.
3
Convert loan to mudarabah
Immediately after, the capital owner takes the same amount back as mudarabah capital. Now the worker holds the money as mudarib but remains liable for the original loan.
The two contracts are separate but sequential.
4
Analyze liability outcomes
If profit is made, it is shared as per mudarabah terms, and the capital owner recovers his capital as repayment of the loan. If loss occurs or capital is destroyed, the worker must still repay the loan, thus the capital is guaranteed.
The loan liability survives regardless of mudarabah outcome.
5
Alternative using 'inan partnership
A second method: give all capital except one dirham as loan, contract an 'inan partnership, then give the dirham. The worker uses the entire amount; loss falls on him due to the loan.
The one dirham exception avoids making the entire capital a loan initially.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وقد ذكر الشارح الزيلعي في أول كتاب المضاربة عند قوله والمضارب أمين الخ ما نصه : وإذا أراد أن يجعله عليه مضموناً أقرضه رأس المال كله وأشهد عليه وسلمه إليه ثم يأخذه منه مضاربة ثم يدفعه إلى المستقرض يستعين به في العمل، فإذا عمل وربح كان الربح بينهما على الشرط وأخذ رأس المال على أنه بدل القرض وإن لم يربح أخذ رأس المال بالقرض. وإن هلك هلك على المستقرض وهو العامل أو أقرضه كله إلا در هما منه وسلمه إليه وعقدا شركة العنان ثم يدفع إليه الدرهم ويعمل فيه المستقرض، فإن بينهما على ما شرطا وإن هلك هلك عليه . اهـ كلام الزيلعي وهو صريح في أن اشتراط العمل (١) قوله: (في العمل أي فيكون المال عنده بضاعة وهال جائز كما في المتون اهـ منه.
This and the commentator al-Zayla'i mentioned at the beginning of the book of mudarabah at his saying 'And the mudarib is trustworthy' etc., his text: 'And if he wants to make it guaranteed upon him, he gives him the entire capital as a loan and has witnesses and delivers it to him, then takes it from him as mudarabah, then gives it to the borrower to use in work. Then if he works and makes profit, the profit is between them according to the condition, and he takes the capital as the substitute for the loan. If he does not profit, he takes the capital as the loan. If it is destroyed, it is destroyed upon the borrower, who is the worker. Or he gives him the entire capital except one dirham from it and delivers it to him and they contract an 'inan partnership, then he gives him the dirham and the borrower works in it. Then it is between them as they stipulated, and if it is destroyed, it is destroyed upon him.' End of al-Zayla'i's speech. And it is explicit that stipulating work... (Footnote: His word 'in the work' means the wealth is with him as merchandise and it is permissible as in the texts. From it.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents a legal stratagem (ḥīlah) from al-Zayla'i to circumvent the general rule that the mudarib (worker) is an amīn (trustee) and not liable for capital loss. To make the capital guaranteed (maḍmūn), the capital owner first gives the capital as a qarḍ (loan), making the worker a debtor. Then he immediately takes it back as mudarabah capital. Now if the capital is lost, it is the worker's liability because it was a loan. The profit is shared as per their mudarabah agreement. An alternative stratagem using an 'inan partnership with a single dirham is also described. This highlights the Hanafi tradition of applying legal reasoning to achieve practical results while staying within the framework of the Sharia.

Key Terms
حيلة (ḥīlah): A legal stratagem that achieves a permissible outcome by combining valid contracts in sequence.
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership where one provides capital and the other provides labor, profit shared by agreement; loss is borne by capital owner.
قرض (qarḍ): A loan contract where the borrower is obliged to repay the exact amount borrowed.
شركة العنان (shirkat al-'inan): An 'inan partnership where both partners contribute capital and work; profits are shared as agreed, losses are proportional to capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ḥīlah described by al-Zayla'i, how can the capital owner make the worker liable for the capital?
A) By stipulating liability in the mudarabah contract
B) By first giving the capital as a loan, then taking it back as mudarabah
C) By having the worker sign a guarantee
D) It is not possible to make the worker liable

Key Takeaway
The ḥīlah uses a loan to transform the mudarib from trustee to debtor, ensuring the capital is guaranteed.

Partnership After Capital Destruction: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on matn ruling about purchase when other's capital destroyed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the effect of capital destruction after a purchase in a partnership, explain the difference between contractual and ownership partnership, and apply the reconciliation via explicit agency.

Core Idea
A purchase made during a valid partnership is not undone by later capital loss; the dispute is about the basis of sharing—contract or ownership.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in partnership (shirkah): one partner uses his own funds to buy an item, and then the other partner's capital is destroyed. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Imam Muhammad sees the partnership as a contract, while Hasan b. Ziyad views it as mere co-ownership. The commentator reconciles the views by the presence or absence of explicit agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the matn ruling
Read the matn: 'If one of them buys with his own property and the property of the other perishes, then the purchased item is between them according to their condition.' This sets the general rule that the purchase is shared per the partnership terms.
The matn uses 'according to their condition', which hints at the contractual nature.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Muhammad holds that the partnership is a contract (sharikat al-'aqd), so profit-sharing follows the contract terms. Hasan b. Ziyad holds that the partnership becomes ownership (sharikat al-milk) once capital is destroyed, so profit is by ownership shares.
This difference affects whether the contract terms still govern after the loss.
3
Analyze the role of agency
The commentator notes that the word 'and' in 'and perishes' actually means 'then', establishing a sequence: first the loss, then the purchase. If explicit agency was granted in the partnership contract, the agency survives even if the partnership contract is voided, so the purchase remains shared.
Explicit agency (wakalah) keeps the purchase shared even in Hasan's view.
4
Apply the reconciliation
If the partners only had a general partnership without explicit agency, the purchase belongs solely to the buyer because the implied agency is voided with the contract. If they explicitly stated agency, the purchase is shared as co-ownership, and the buyer recovers his share of the price from the other.
This reconciles the two views by introducing a condition.
5
Work through the example from al-Muhit
Consider a partnership with capital: 100 dinars (value 1500) and 1000 dirhams. The dirham-owner buys a slave girl, then dinars are destroyed. The slave is shared in fifths (3/5 for dinar-owner, 2/5 for dirham-owner) according to capital at purchase time. The buyer recovers 3/5 of the price from the other.
This example assumes the partnership existed at purchase; the profit is divided by capital shares, not contract terms, aligning with the ownership view but reconciled by agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن اشترى أحدهما بماله وهلك مال الآخر فالمشتري بينهما) يعني على ما شرطا لأن الملك حين وقع وقع مشتركاً بينهما لقيام الشركة وقت الشراء فلا يتغير الحكم بهلاك مال الآخر بعد ذلك. وإنما لم يقل على ما شرطا للاختلاف في هذه الشركة فعند محمد هي عقد فيكون الربح على ما شرطا وأيهما باع جاز بيعه لأن الشركة قد تمت في المشتري فلا تنقض بهلاك المال بعد تمامها، وعند الحسن بن زياد هي شركة ملك لأن شركة العقد قد بطلت بهلاك المال كما لو هلك قبل الشراء وإنما بقي ما هو حكم الشراء وهو واعلم أن الواو في قوله وهلك» بمعنى «ثم لأنه لو هلك مال أحدهما ثم اشترى الآخر بالمال رحا بالوكالة في عقد الشركة فالمشتري مشترك بينهما على ما شرطا لأن الشركة إن بطلت فالوكالة المصرح بها قائمة وكان مشتركاً بحكم الوكالة وتكون شركة ملك ويرجع على شريكه بحصته من الثمن، وإن ذكرا مجرد الشركة ولم ينصا على الوكالة فيها كان المشتري للذي اشتراه خاصة لأن الوقوع على الشركة حكم الوكالة التي تضمنتها الشركة، فإذا بطلت يبطل ما في ضمنها بخلاف ما إذا صرحا بها على ما ذكر قوله : (ورجع على شريكه بحصته منه أي من الثمن لأنه وكيل في حصة شريكه وقد قضى الثمن من ماله فيرجع عليه بحسابه لعدم الرضا بدون ضمانه. وفي المحيط : لأحدهما مائة دينار قيمتها ألف وخمسمائة وللآخر ألف درهم فاشتركتا عناناً وشرطا الربح والوضيعة على رأس المال فاشترى صاحب الدراهم جارية ثم هلكت الدنانير فالجارية بينهما وربحها أخماساً؛ ثلاثة أخماسه لصاحب الدنانير وخمسان لصاحب الدراهم لما بينا أن حال شرائها كانت الشركة قائمة وبهلاك أحد المالين لا تنتقض الشركة والربح يقسم على قدر ماليهما يوم الشراء، ومقدار رأس ماليهما يوم الشراء على خمسة أسهم خمسان لأحدهما وثلاثة أخماسه للآخر، ويرجع صاحب الدراهم على الآخر بثلاثة أخماس الألف لأنه صار وكيلاً عن صاحبه بالشراء في ثلاثة أخماس الجارية وقد نقد ثمن ذلك من ماله ولو كان على عكسه رجع صاحب الدنانير عليه بخمسي الثمن أربعون ديناراً لما عرف فإن اشترى صاحب الدنانير بها غلاماً والآخر بألفه جارية وقبضا وهلكا يهلكان من مالهما لأن كل واحد حينما اشترى كانت الشركة بينهما قائمة وتمامه فيه
His statement: (If one of them buys with his own property and the property of the other perishes, then the purchased item is between them) meaning according to their condition, because ownership when it occurred was shared between them due to the existence of the partnership at the time of purchase, so the ruling does not change by the perishing of the other's property afterwards. He did not say 'according to their condition' because of a difference regarding this partnership: according to Muhammad it is a contract, so profit is according to their condition, and whichever sells his sale is valid because the partnership is completed in the purchased item, so it is not invalidated by the perishing of property after completion. According to al-Hasan b. Ziyad it is a partnership of ownership because the contractual partnership was invalidated by the perishing of property as if it perished before purchase, and only the ruling of purchase remains. Know that the waw in his statement 'and perishes' is in the sense of 'then' (thumma), because if the property of one perishes then the other buys with property as an agent in the partnership contract, then the purchased item is shared between them according to their condition because if the partnership is invalidated the explicit agency remains, so he is a partner by virtue of agency and it becomes a partnership of ownership, and he recovers from his partner his share of the price. And if they mentioned only the partnership and did not state agency in it, then the purchased item belongs specifically to the one who bought it because the occurrence upon partnership is a ruling of the agency that the partnership implied; so when it is invalidated, what is within it is invalidated, contrary to when they explicitly state agency. His statement: (And he recovers from his partner his share of it) i.e. from the price, because he is an agent for his partner's share and he paid the price from his own property, so he recovers from him his share due to lack of consent without guarantee. In al-Muhit: One has 100 dinars worth 1500 and the other has 1000 dirhams, they form an 'inan partnership and stipulate profit and loss according to capital. The owner of the dirhams buys a slave girl, then the dinars are destroyed. The slave girl is between them and its profit is in fifths: three-fifths for the owner of the dinars and two-fifths for the owner of the dirhams, because we have explained that at the time of purchase the partnership was existing, and the partnership is not invalidated by the destruction of one of the capitals. Profit is divided according to their capital on the day of purchase. The amount of their capital on the day of purchase is five shares: two shares for one and three shares for the other. The owner of the dirhams recovers from the other three-fifths of the thousand because he became an agent for his partner in buying three-fifths of the slave girl and he paid the price from his property. If the reverse, the owner of the dinars recovers from him two-fifths of the price, forty dinars. If the owner of the dinars buys a slave with them and the other buys a slave girl with his thousand, and they take delivery and they perish, they perish from their own property because when each bought the partnership was existing between them.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn ruling about a specific scenario in partnership: one partner uses his own money to buy an item, and then the other partner's capital is destroyed. The commentator first explains that the purchase is shared according to their condition because the partnership existed at the time of purchase. He notes a difference of opinion between Imam Muhammad, who considers the partnership a contract (so the ruling follows the contract terms), and al-Hasan b. Ziyad, who considers it a partnership of ownership (so the contract is voided by the loss of capital, but the purchase stands as shared). The commentary then clarifies that the word 'and' (waw) in the matn actually means 'then' (ثم), emphasizing the sequence: first the other's capital perishes, then the partner buys. If the partnership is voided by the loss, but there is explicit agency, the purchase is still shared because the agency continues. If only partnership was mentioned without explicit agency, the purchase belongs solely to the buyer. The passage then explains the reimbursement rule: the buying partner recovers his share of the price from the other because he acted as agent. An example from al-Muhit is given: a partnership with unequal capitals (100 dinars worth 1500 vs 1000 dirhams), profit-sharing agreed according to capital. The dirham-owner buys a slave girl, then the dinars are destroyed. The slave girl is shared in proportion to the capital values at the time of purchase (fifths), and the buyer recovers his share of the price. This illustrates the practical application of the earlier ruling.

Key Terms
شركة العقد (sharikat al-'aqd): A partnership established by contract, with mutual agency and sharing of profit/loss according to agreement.
شركة ملك (sharikat al-milk): Co-ownership arising from a common event (e.g., inheritance) or from a voided contract; no mutual agency.
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; one partner acting as agent for the other in the purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two partners form an 'inan partnership, and one partner buys a slave with his own money, then the other partner's capital is destroyed after the purchase, according to Imam Muhammad:
A) The slave belongs solely to the buyer.
B) The slave is shared between the partners according to their condition.
C) The slave is shared, but profit is divided according to ownership shares only.
D) The partnership is automatically voided and the slave is returned.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a purchase made during a valid partnership is not invalidated by later capital loss; the sharing basis depends on whether the partnership is contractual or with explicit agency.

8 min
Purchase Disputes and Invalid Conditions in 'Inan Partnership
Ruling on conflicting claims and invalid conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the buyer's statement is accepted in a partnership purchase dispute and explain why a fixed profit condition does not void the partnership.

Core Idea
A partner's word is believed in a purchase dispute; an invalid profit condition is void but the partnership remains valid.

In an 'inan partnership, conflicts can arise over whether a purchase belongs to the partnership or the individual, and what happens if partners stipulate a fixed profit. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq provides clear rulings on both issues, rooted in the principles of agency and the Hanafi treatment of invalid conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Read the first part from al-Khaniyya: two partners, one buys goods. The other claims it's for the partnership; the buyer claims it's for himself. Recognise this as a conflict of claims.
The buyer is a free agent – this is key.
2
Apply the default rule
The buyer's statement is accepted with his oath because he is acting for himself. Understand the rationale: he is not an agent here unless proven otherwise.
This is a procedural rule, not a substantive one.
3
Analyse the fatwa incident
Consider the case where the buyer says the purchase is for the partnership and demands reimbursement. The other partner says the price came from partnership funds. Determine that the buyer's claim of payment from his own money is a claim of discharge requiring proof.
Admission of partnership purchase shifts the burden.
4
Identify the invalid profit condition
Locate where the text states: 'It is invalid if a specific amount of dirhams is stipulated for one of them from the profit.' Understand that this condition is invalid because it cuts off the other partner's right to share in profit.
Analogy with muzara'ah (sharecropping).
5
Understand the effect on the partnership
The invalid condition does not void the partnership. The condition is removed, and profit is divided according to capital or valid terms. The reason: partnerships contain the meaning of agency, and agency contracts are not invalidated by invalid conditions.
Cite al-Fatawa al-Sughra and Khwahar Zada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخانية : وإذا اشتركا شركة عنان فاشترى أحدهما متاعاً فقال الشريك الآخر هو من شركتنا، وقال المشتري هو لي خاصة اشتريته بمالي لنفسي قبل الشركة كان القول قول المشتري لأنه حر يعمل لنفسه فيما اشترى فيكون القول قوله مع يمينه بالله تعالى ما هو من شركتهما .اهـ. أقول: وقد وقعت حادثة الفتوى : اشترى أحدهما متاعاً وقال هو للشركة وقد دفعت ثمنه من مالي لأرجع عليك بحصتك من الثمن فقال الآخر دفعت ثمنه من مال الشركة ولا رجوع لك علي، والذي يظهر أن القول قول المشتري لما ذكر قاضيخان أنه حر الخ. وذلك لأنه لما صدقه في الشراء ثبت الشراء للشركة وبه يثبت نصف الثمن بذمته، وقوله دفعت من مال الشركة دعوى وفائه فلا يقبل بلا بينة ولذلك قالوا : فإن كان شراؤه لا يعرف إلا بقوله فعليه الحجة لأنه يدعي وجوب المال في ذمة الآخر وهو ينكر وهنا ليس منكراً بل مقر بالشراء الموجب لتعلق الثمن بذمته، وإذا طلب اليمين أنه ما دفعه من مال الشركة فله ذلك تأمل. رملي . قوله : ولو اشترى من جنس تجارتهما وأشهد (الخ أقول : في فتاوى قارئ الهداية ما نصه : إذا اشترى أحد الشريكين عيناً ونقد الثمن من مال الشركة ثم ادعى مشتراه لنفسه على شريكه بحصته منه وتفسد إن شرط لأحدهما دراهم مسماة من الربح ولكل من التناقض الواقع في جواب المسألة حيث قال محمد في بعض المواضع فاشترى بالمال الباقي بعد ذلك يكون لصاحبها، وفي بعضها إذا اشترى الآخر بماله بعد ذلك يكون بينهما فجعل محمل الأول ما إذا لم يكن في الشركة وكالة مصرح بها، ومحمل الثاني إذا صرحا بها على ما ذكر قوله : (وتفسد أن شرط لأحدهما دراهم مسماة من الربح) لأنه شرط يوجب انقطاع حق الشركة فعساه لا يخرج إلا القدر المسمى لأحدها، ونظيره في المزارعة إذا اشترط لأحدهما قفزاناً مسماة. وفي الخانية ولو تفاوتا في المال في شركة العنان وشرطا الربح والوضيعة نصفين قال في الكتاب الشركة فاسدة قالوا: لم يرد محمد بهذا فساد العقد وإنما أراد به فساد شرط الوضيعة لأن الشركة لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، وكذا لو شرطا الوضيعة على المضارب كان فاسداً .اهـ. وهذا صريح في أن الذي يبطل بالشرط الفاسد إنما هو الشرط لا الشركة . قال في الفتاوى الصغرى وذكر خواهر زاده في أول المضاربة الشركات لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة لأن فيها معنى الوكالة والوكالات لا تبطل بالشروط، وإذا شرط في المضاربة ربح عشرة أو في الشركة تبطل لا لأنه شرط فاسد بل لأنه شرط تنتفي به الشركة وعسى أن يجري على إطلاقه من أن الشركات والمضاربات لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة اهـ . خاصة فهل يقبل قوله أو لا؟ أجاب أن كانت شركة عنان وله بينة تشهد أنه عند العقد صرح بالشراء لنفسه خصوصاً فالمشتري له وإن لم يكن له بينة فإن نقد من مال شريكه فالمشتري على الشركة اهـ. فتأمل. ورأيت بخط بعض العلماء أن ما ذكره قارئ الهداية لم يستند فيه إلى نقل فلا يعارض ما في المحيط اهـ. ويمكن الجواب بحمل ما في فتاوى قارئ الهداية على ما إذا لم يكن من جنس تجارتهما
Al-Khaniyya: Two persons enter into an 'inan partnership, then one buys goods. The other partner says, 'It is from our partnership,' and the buyer says, 'It is specifically mine; I bought it with my own property for myself before the partnership.' The statement is of the buyer because he is a free agent working for himself in what he bought, so his statement is accepted with his oath by Allah that it is not from their partnership. End. I say: A fatwa incident occurred: One partner bought goods and said, 'It is for the partnership; I paid its price from my own property to recover your share from you.' The other said, 'You paid its price from partnership property; you have no recourse against me.' What appears is that the statement is of the buyer due to what Qadi Khan mentioned that he is free etc. Because when he believed him regarding the purchase, the purchase is established for the partnership, and by that half the price is established as a debt on him. His statement 'I paid from partnership property' is a claim of discharge, so it is not accepted without proof. Therefore they said: If his purchase is known only by his statement, then the burden of proof is on him because he claims an obligation of money on the other's liability while the other denies. Here he is not denier but acknowledges the purchase which necessitates the attachment of the price to his liability. And if he requests the oath that he did not pay from partnership property, he has that. Consider. Al-Ramli. His statement: If he buys from the type of their trade and makes witnesses... I say: In the Fatawa of Qari' al-Hidaya: If one of the partners buys a commodity and pays the price from partnership property, then claims it is for himself specifically... and it is invalid if a specific amount of dirhams is stipulated for one of them from the profit... and regarding the contradiction in the answer to the question: Muhammad said in some places: 'He buys with the remaining property, it belongs to its owner,' and in some: 'If the other buys with his property after that, it is between them.' So I consider the first to be when there is no explicit agency in the partnership, and the second when they explicitly state agency. His statement: (And it is invalid if a specific amount of dirhams is stipulated for one of them from the profit) because it is a condition that cuts off the right of the partnership, so perhaps nothing will come out except the specified amount for that one. Its analogy is in muzara'ah if a specific number of measures is stipulated for one of them. And in al-Khaniyya: If they differ in capital in 'inan partnership and stipulate profit and loss half-half, said in the book: the partnership is invalid. They said: Muhammad did not mean by this the invalidity of the contract, but rather the invalidity of the condition of loss, because the partnership is not invalidated by invalid conditions. Similarly, if they stipulate loss on the mudarib, it is invalid. End. This is explicit that what becomes invalid by an invalid condition is only the condition, not the partnership. In al-Fatawa al-Sughra: Khwahar Zada mentioned at the beginning of mudaraba that partnerships are not invalidated by invalid conditions because they contain the meaning of agency, and agencies are not invalidated by conditions. If a profit of ten is stipulated in mudaraba or in partnership, it is invalid not because it is an invalid condition but because it is a condition that negates the partnership, and perhaps it proceeds on its absolute [principle] that partnerships and mudarabas are not invalidated by invalid conditions. End. Specifically: So, is his statement accepted or not? He answered: If it was an 'inan partnership and he has evidence that at the time of the contract he explicitly stated the purchase for himself specifically, then the purchase is for him. If he does not have evidence, and he paid from the property of his partner, then the purchase is for the partnership. End. Consider. And I saw in the handwriting of some scholars that what Qari' al-Hidaya mentioned is not based on a transmitted source, so it does not contradict what is in al-Muhit. End. And it is possible to answer by interpreting the fatwa of Qari' al-Hidaya to apply when it is not from the type of their trade.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings on partnership disputes and conditions. First, from al-Khaniyya: When one partner buys goods and the other claims it belongs to the partnership, but the buyer claims it is for himself, the buyer is believed with his oath because he is a free agent acting for himself. The author recounts a fatwa incident: a partner buys goods, claims it is for the partnership, and demands reimbursement from the other; the other says the price was paid from partnership funds. The ruling is that the buyer is believed (since he admitted the purchase is for the partnership, establishing a debt on the other), and his claim that he paid from partnership funds is a claim of discharge that requires proof. The second part discusses the matn phrase: 'If he buys from the type of their trade and makes witnesses...' and a fatwa from Qari' al-Hidaya: If a partner buys an item and pays from partnership property, then claims it for himself, the outcome depends on whether he explicitly stated at contract that it was for himself. The passage then discusses a contradiction in Imam Muhammad's answers about purchase after destruction, resolved by the presence or absence of explicit agency. Next, the condition that invalidates the partnership: stipulating a specific amount of profit for one partner. This condition is invalid because it cuts off the partner's right to share in profit beyond that amount. However, the invalid condition does not void the entire partnership; only the condition is voided, as per the principle that partnerships are not invalidated by invalid conditions, since they contain agency. The passage cites al-Khaniyya and al-Fatawa al-Sughra to support that the invalid condition does not nullify the underlying agency contract. Finally, the fatwa from Qari' al-Hidaya is reconciled by limiting it to cases where the purchase is not from the type of trade.

Key Terms
شركة عنان (sharikat 'inan): A general partnership where each partner contributes capital and shares in profit and loss proportionally, with mutual agency.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is legally invalid but does not necessarily void the entire contract; it is removed and the contract remains if possible.
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; the partnership contract inherently includes mutual agency, which is why invalid conditions do not void it.
دعوى وفاء (da'wa wafa'): A claim of discharge or payment of a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi 'inan partnership, the partners stipulate that one will receive a fixed 100 dirhams of profit regardless of actual earnings. What is the ruling on the partnership contract?
A) The partnership contract is completely void.
B) The condition is invalid, but the partnership remains valid.
C) The profit is split equally as per default rules.
D) The partnership is valid only if both agree to remove the condition.

Key Takeaway
In a partnership purchase dispute, the buyer's word stands with oath; an invalid profit condition is void but does not void the partnership because agency survives the condition.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate

Effect of Stipulating Fixed Profit in Partnership
Explaining the ruling on stipulating fixed profit and the intra-Hanafi interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of stipulating a fixed profit for one partner and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Stipulating a fixed profit for one partner does not invalidate the partnership; only the condition is void.

Partnership contracts are built on mutual agency. When partners include an invalid condition—like a fixed profit for one—does the whole contract collapse? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq navigates an apparent contradiction in Muhammad al-Shaybani's statements and settles on the principle that partnerships survive invalid conditions, just as agency does.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition at issue
Find the exact condition: stipulating 'named dirhams' (fixed amount) from the profit for one partner. This is the controversial condition.
The passage calls it 'shart fāsid' (invalid condition).
2
Note the apparent contradiction in Muhammad's statements
In some places Muhammad says 'the partnership is invalid' (fasid); in other contexts he implies it is valid. Determine what he intended.
The contradiction is resolved by interpreting 'fasid' as referring to the condition, not the contract.
3
Apply the principle of agency
Partnerships contain the meaning of agency (wakala). Agencies are not invalidated by void conditions. Therefore, the partnership remains valid despite the invalid condition.
This is the reasoning given by Khwaharzada and others.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that the partnership is valid; only the condition is void. Profits are then distributed according to capital ratio, not the fixed amount.
This is supported by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على شريكه بحصته منه وتفسد إن شرط لأحدهما دراهم مسماة من الربح ولكل من التناقض الواقع في جواب المسألة حيث قال محمد في بعض المواضع فاشترى بالمال الباقي بعد ذلك يكون لصاحبها، وفي بعضها إذا اشترى الآخر بماله بعد ذلك يكون بينهما فجعل محمل الأول ما إذا لم يكن في الشركة وكالة مصرح بها، ومحمل الثاني إذا صرحا بها على ما ذكر قوله : (ورجع على شريكه بحصته منه أي من الثمن لأنه وكيل في حصة شريكه وقد قضى الثمن تجارتهما
On his partner for his share from it, and it becomes invalid if he stipulates for one of them named dirhams from the profit, and for each of the contradiction appearing in the answer of the issue where Muhammad said in some places: 'he bought with the remaining wealth after that it belongs to its owner', and in some of them: 'if the other bought with his wealth after that it is between them'. He made the interpretation of the first as when there is no explicit agency in the partnership, and the interpretation of the second as when they explicitly mentioned it, as mentioned. His saying: 'and he has recourse against his partner for his share from it', i.e., from the price, because he is an agent for his partner's share and he has paid the price from his own wealth, so he has recourse against him for his amount due to lack of consent without his guarantee. And in al-Muhit: 'For one of them is one hundred dinars worth one thousand five hundred, and for the other one thousand dirhams, and they entered into a partnership of 'inan and stipulated profit and loss on the capital. Then the owner of the dirhams bought a slave-girl, then the dinars perished. So the slave-girl is between them, and her profit in fifths: three-fifths for the owner of the dinars and two-fifths for the owner of the dirhams, because as we stated, at the time of her purchase the partnership was existing, and with the destruction of one of the two capitals the partnership is not dissolved, and the profit is divided according to their capitals on the day of purchase. And the amount of their capitals on the day of purchase is five shares: two-fifths for one and three-fifths for the other. And the owner of the dirhams has recourse against the other for three-fifths of the thousand because he became an agent for his partner in purchasing three-fifths of the slave-girl and he has paid the price of that from his wealth. And had it been the opposite, the owner of the dinars would have recourse against him for two-fifths of the price, forty dinars, as known. Then if the owner of the dinars buys with them a slave and the other with his thousand a slave-girl, and they take possession and they perish, they perish from their wealth because each one at the time of purchase the partnership was existing between them, and its completion is therein.' His saying: 'and it becomes invalid that he stipulates for one of them named dirhams from the profit', because it is a condition that necessitates cutting off the right of partnership, so that nothing comes out except the named amount for one of them. And its analogy in sharecropping is if he stipulates for one of them named qafizes. And in al-Khaniyya: 'If they differ in wealth in a partnership of 'inan and they stipulate profit and loss half-half, it is said in the book: the partnership is invalid.' They said: 'Muhammad did not mean by this the invalidity of the contract, but rather he meant the invalidity of the condition of loss, because the partnership is not annulled by invalid conditions.' Similarly, if they stipulate loss on the mudarib, it is invalid. This is explicit that what is annulled by an invalid condition is only the condition, not the partnership. He said in al-Fatawa al-Sughra: 'And Khwaharzada mentioned at the beginning of mudaraba: partnerships are not annulled by invalid conditions because they contain the meaning of agency, and agencies are not annulled by conditions. And if one stipulates in mudaraba a profit of ten or in partnership, it becomes invalid not because it is an invalid condition, but because it is a condition by which the partnership is negated, and it may be taken in its absoluteness that partnerships and mudarabas are not annulled by invalid conditions.' End. 'Special case: then is his statement accepted or not?' He answered: 'If it is a partnership of 'inan and he has evidence that at the contract he explicitly stated the purchase for himself specifically, then the purchased item is for him. And if he has no evidence, then if he paid from the wealth of his partner, the purchased item is on the partnership.' End. So reflect. And I saw in the handwriting of some scholars that what the reader of al-Hidaya mentioned is not based on a transmission, so it does not contradict what is in al-Muhit. And it can be answered by interpreting what is in the fatwas of the reader of al-Hidaya as when it is not of the type of their trade.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of stipulating a fixed amount of profit for one partner in a partnership. The author first explains the ruling of recourse: if one partner pays the full price from his own wealth, he can claim reimbursement from his partner for the latter's share, because he acts as an agent. Then, using an example from al-Muhit, he illustrates how profits are divided in proportion to capital shares at the time of purchase, and how the paying partner can reclaim the portion paid for his partner. The core issue arises when a condition stipulates a fixed profit (e.g., named dirhams) for one partner. If such a condition is included, the partnership is not invalidated—only the condition is void, based on the principle that partnerships are akin to agency and are not annulled by invalid conditions. This is a point of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school: some early statements suggested the partnership is invalid, but the preferred view is that the partnership remains valid. The passage also addresses a subsidiary issue: if a partner claims he bought goods for himself, not for the partnership, his statement is accepted if he has evidence; otherwise, if he used partnership funds, the goods belong to the partnership.

Key Terms
شركة العنان (shirkat al-ʿinān): A type of partnership where partners contribute capital but each is an agent for the other within their trade, with equal or unequal shares, and profits are distributed according to agreement, but loss is borne in proportion to capital.
شرط فاسد (sharṭ fāsid): A condition that violates the requirements of the contract but does not necessarily invalidate the contract itself, especially in partnerships which are based on agency.
وكالة (wakāla): Agency; one person authorizes another to act on his behalf in a specific matter. The passage uses it to explain why partnerships are not easily invalidated: because they contain the element of agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi partnership, if the partners stipulate a fixed amount of profit for one partner, what is the effect on the partnership contract?
A) The partnership becomes invalid and must be dissolved.
B) The partnership remains valid but the condition is void.
C) The partnership becomes voidable at the option of the disadvantaged partner.
D) The condition is valid and must be fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
A condition stipulating fixed profit for one partner is void, but the partnership contract itself remains valid because partnerships share the legal nature of agency.

Permissible Actions of a Partner: The Five Customary Transactions
Listing and justifying five permissible actions for partners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five actions a partner in a Hanafi partnership may undertake and explain the rationales (custom, a fortiori, analogy) for each.

Core Idea
A partner may conduct customary trade transactions because partnership aims at profit, not restriction.

In Hanafi fiqh, a partnership (shirkah) is formed to trade and earn profit. But what can a partner independently do with partnership capital without explicit permission? This lesson unpacks the matn of Kanz al-Daqāʾiq, which lists five actions a partner may perform. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq provides justifications rooted in custom (ʿurf) and legal reasoning, and notes an internal disagreement on mudāraba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five permissible actions
From the matn: bidaʿa (giving capital as gratuitous agency), istīʾjār (hiring), īdāʿ (deposit), mudāraba (profit-sharing investment), and tawkīl (appointing agents).
These are all common in trade.
2
Understand the justification for each
Bidaʿa and hiring are customary; deposit is a fortiori (even more permissible) because it is gratuitous; mudāraba is a lower form of partnership; agency is an accessory to trade.
Custom (ʿurf) plays a key role in justifying these actions.
3
Note the internal dispute on mudāraba
A report from Abū Ḥanīfa disallows mudāraba because it is a type of partnership. But the preferred view (riwāyat al-aṣl) allows it, since the aim is profit, not partnership per se.
The tarjīḥ in al-Hidāya favors permissibility.
4
Distinguish mudāraba from mushāraka
A partner may do mudāraba (giving capital to an agent) but may not form another partnership (mushāraka) without the partner's permission, as per al-Jawhara.
Mudāraba is a subordinate arrangement, while mushāraka creates a new partnership.
5
Apply the rule to agency
Appointing agents is allowed because partnership is for trade, unlike a specific purchase agency which does not entail delegation.
The ḥukm differs based on the scope of the original contract.

Source Text

لكل من شريكي العنان والمفاوضة أن يبضع ويستأجر ويودع ويضارب ويوكل ويده في المال قوله: (ولكل من شريكي العنان والمفاوضة أن يبضع ويستأجر ويودع ويضارب ويوكل) بيان لما لكل منهما أن يفعله؛ أما البضاعة فلأنها معتادة في عقد الشركة. وفي القاموس الباضع الشريك والجمع بضع من بضع كمنع بضوعاً .اهـ. والمراد هنا دفع المال لآخر ليعمل فيه على أن يكون الربح لرب المال ولا شيء للعامل، وأما الاستئجار فلكونه معتاداً بين التجار وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا استأجر رجلاً ليتجر له أو ليحفظ المال، وأما الإيداع فجوازه بالأولى لأنه استحفاظ بغير أجر، وأما المضاربة فلكونها دون الشركة فتتضمنها. وعن أبي حنيفة ليس له ذلك لأنه نوع شركة والأول أصح وهو رواية الأصل لأن الشركة غير مقصودة وإنما المقصود تحصيل الربح كما إذا استأجره بأجر بل أولى لأنه تحصيل بدون ضمان ذمته بخلاف الشركة حيث لا يملكها لأن الشيء لا يستتبع مثله؛ كذا في الهداية. وبهذا علم أنه ليس للشريك أن يشارك بخلاف المضاربة ولذا قال ويضارب» ولم يقل ويشارك». قال في الجوهرة إلا بإذن شريكه. وأما التوكيل فلأنه من توابع التجارة والشركة انعقدت للتجارة بخلاف الوكيل بالشراء حيث لا يملك أن يوكل غيره لأنه عقد خاص طلب منه تحصيل المعين فلا يستتبع مثله. ولم يذكر المصنف بقية أحكام الشريك وهي مهمة فمنها العارية. قال الحاكم في الكافي وليس له أن يعير في القياس فإن فعل؛ فإن أعار دابة فعطبت تحت المستعير فالقياس فيه أن المعير ضامن لنصف قيمة الدابة لشريكه ولكني أستحسن أن لا أضمنه، وهذا قياس قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد، وكذلك لو أعار ثوباً أو داراً أو خادماً اهـ. ومنها الرهن فإن كان شريك عنان فليس له ذلك قال الكرخي في مختصره قال محمد في كتاب الرهن إذا رهن أحد شريكي العنان متاعاً من الشركة بدين عليهما لم يجز ضامناً للرهن، ولو ارتهن بدين لهما أداناه وقبض لم يجز على شريكه من قبل أنه لم يرتهن، فإن هلك الرهن وقيمته والدين سواء ذهب بحصته ويرجع شريكه بحصته وكان يسلطه أن على المطلوب ويرجع المطلوب بنصف قيمة الرهن على المرتهن وإن شاء شريك المرتهن ضمن شريكه حصته من الدين لأن هلاك الرهن في يده بمنزلة الاستيفاء ثم قال بعده: ويجوز لأحد المتفاوضين أن يرهن ويرتهن على شريكه ؛ كذا في غاية البيان. وفي المحيط : لا أحدهما يرهن شيئاً من الشركة بدين عليه إلا بإذن شريكه، وكذا لا يرتهن رهناً بدين من الشركة في نصيب شريكه إلا إذا ولي عقده أو يأمر من يوليه اهـ. وفي الخانية : ولمن ولي المبايعة أن يرهن بالثمن. ومنها ليس له أن يكاتب لأنه ليس من عادة التجار؛ كذا في الجوهرة. وكذا ليس له الأمة وقضاء الدين كما في المحيط . ومنها ما إذا أخذ أحدهما مالاً مضاربة فالربح له فيحصل التوفيق تأمل. قوله : وبهذا) علم أنه ليس للشريك أن يشارك ليس هذا على إطلاقه كما سينبه عليه المؤلف بعد ورقة .
For each of the two partners of ʿinān and mufāwaḍa: he may engage in bidaʿa, hire, deposit, enter into mudāraba, and appoint agents, with his hand in the wealth. His saying: 'And for each of the two partners of ʿinān and mufāwaḍa, he may engage in bidaʿa, hire, deposit, enter into mudāraba, and appoint agents' is an explanation of what each may do. As for bidaʿa, because it is customary in the contract of partnership. And in al-Qāmūs: al-bāḍiʿ is the partner, plural buḍʻ from baḍaʿa like manaʻa buḍūʻan. End. And what is meant here is giving wealth to another to work with it on condition that the profit is for the owner of the wealth and nothing for the worker. As for hiring, because it is customary among merchants, and he made it general so it includes if he hires a man to trade for him or to preserve the wealth. As for deposit, its permissibility is a fortiori because it is safekeeping without compensation. As for mudāraba, because it is lesser than partnership and thus includes it. And it is related from Abū Ḥanīfa that he does not have that because it is a type of partnership, but the first is more correct and it is the transmission of the original, because the partnership is not intended; rather, what is intended is earning profit, as if he hired him for wages, indeed more so because it is earning without liability of his liability, unlike partnership where he does not own it because a thing does not entail its like; thus in al-Hidāya. And by this it is known that the partner may not enter into a partnership (mushāraka) unlike mudāraba, hence he said 'and he may enter into mudāraba' and did not say 'and he may enter into partnership'. He said in al-Jawhara: except with the permission of his partner. As for appointment of agents, because it is among the accessories of trade, and the partnership was contracted for trade, unlike an agent for purchase who may not appoint another because it is a specific contract asking for the acquisition of a specific thing, so it does not entail its like. And the author did not mention the remaining rulings of the partner, and they are important. Among them is lending. Al-Ḥākim said in al-Kāfī: He may not lend according to analogy; if he does, then if he lends an animal and it is destroyed under the borrower, the analogy is that the lender is guarantor for half the value of the animal for his partner, but I consider it good (istiḥsān) not to make him liable. This is the analogy of the saying of Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, and Muḥammad. Similarly, if he lends a garment, a house, or a servant. Among them is pledge (rahn). If he is a partner of ʿinān, he does not have that. Al-Karkhī said in his Mukhtaṣar: Muḥammad said in Kitāb al-Rahn: If one of the two partners of ʿinān pledges a commodity from the partnership for a debt owed by them both, it is not valid, and he is a guarantor for the pledge. And if he takes a pledge for a debt owed to them both, which they both lent, and he takes possession, it is not valid regarding his partner because he did not take the pledge. Then if the pledge perishes, and its value and the debt are equal, he loses his share, and his partner has recourse for his share against the debtor, and the debtor has recourse for half the value of the pledge against the pledgee. And if the partner of the pledgee wishes, he can make his partner liable for his share of the debt because the destruction of the pledge in his hand is like collection. Then he said after that: It is permissible for one of the mufāwaḍa partners to pledge and take a pledge on behalf of his partner. Thus in Ghāyat al-Bayān. And in al-Muḥīṭ: Neither of them may pledge anything from the partnership for a debt owed by him except with the permission of his partner. Similarly, he may not take a pledge for a debt from the partnership regarding his partner's share unless he conducts the contract or orders someone to do it. And in al-Khāniyya: For the one who conducts the sale, he may pledge for the price. Among them: He may not enter into a contract of kitāba (manumission by contract) because it is not among the customs of merchants; thus in al-Jawhara. Similarly, he may not marry a slave-girl or pay a debt, as in al-Muḥīṭ. Among them: If one of them takes wealth as mudāraba, the profit is for him, thereby harmony is achieved. Reflect. His saying: 'And by this it is known that the partner may not enter into a partnership (mushāraka)' — this is not absolute, as the author will alert to after a folio.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage delineates the scope of a partner's authority in a partnership (both ʿinān and mufāwaḍa). The author opens by listing five actions a partner may undertake: bidaʿa (giving capital to another to trade with, keeping profit for the owner), hiring (istiʾjār, e.g., hiring an employee for trade or preservation), deposit (īdāʿ, safekeeping without charge), mudāraba (a form of profit-sharing partnership where the partner acts as investor, giving funds to an agent), and appointment of agents (tawkīl, delegating authority). Justifications are provided for each: bidaʿa is customary; hiring is common among merchants; deposit is permissible a fortiori since it is gratuitous; mudāraba is a lower level of partnership and thus is included; agency is essential for trade. There is a reported disagreement from Abū Ḥanīfa that a partner may not engage in mudāraba because it is itself a partnership, but the preferred view (based on the original transmission) allows it, since the aim is profit, not partnership per se. The author also notes that a partner may not form another partnership (mushāraka) without permission, unlike mudāraba. Apostile clarifies this restriction is not absolute, as the author will mention later. The passage then covers additional rulings not in the matn: lending (ʿāriyya) is disallowed by analogy, but istiḥsān exempts from liability; pledge (rahn) is prohibited for ʿinān partners without permission but allowed for mufāwaḍa partners; a partner cannot enter a kitāba contract, marry a slave-girl, or pay a debt unilaterally. Finally, if a partner takes funds as mudāraba, the profit is his.

Key Terms
بضاعة (biḍāʿa): Giving capital to another to trade with, with the condition that all profit goes to the capital owner and the worker gets nothing (like a gratuitous agency).
مضاربة (muḍāraba): A contract where one party (rabb al-mal) provides capital to another (mudarib) to trade, and profits are shared according to a pre-agreed ratio; losses are borne by the capital owner.
مفاوضة (mufāwaḍa): A full partnership where partners have equal capital, equal profit shares, and equal liability, and are also agents and sureties for each other in all matters.
عنان (ʿinān): A limited partnership where partners contribute capital and share profits but are not agents or sureties for each other except in limited respects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT among the five actions a partner may undertake according to the matn?
A) Bidaʿa
B) Lending (ʿāriyya)
C) Hiring (istīʾjār)
D) Mudāraba

Key Takeaway
A partner in a Hanafi partnership may perform five customary trade transactions (bidaʿa, hiring, deposit, mudāraba, agency) without explicit permission, as the partnership is aimed at profit.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
10 min
Additional Rulings: Restrictions on Lending, Pledge, and Other Transactions
Supplementary rulings on partner's restrictions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the restrictions on a partner regarding lending (ʿāriyya), pledge (rahn), kitāba, marrying a slave-girl, and paying debts, and explain the role of istiḥsān in the lending ruling.

Core Idea
A partner may not lend partnership assets without permission, and pledge is heavily restricted for ʿinān partners, though mufāwaḍa partners have broader authority.

The matn of Kanz al-Daqāʾiq only lists five permissible actions, but there are many other important rulings for partners. This lesson explores supplementary rulings from the Hanafi commentaries: lending, pledge, kitāba, and others. These rulings are derived from analogy (qiyās) and sometimes modified by istiḥsān, as seen in the case of lending.

Guided Path
1
Identify the additional rulings discussed
The passage covers lending (ʿāriyya), pledge (rahn), kitāba (manumission contract), marrying a slave-girl, and paying debts. Also, a note on mudāraba profit.
These are all actions not included in the matn but addressed in commentaries.
2
Understand the ruling on lending
By qiyās, a partner who lends partnership property without permission and it perishes is liable to the partner for half the value. But istiḥsān exempts him from liability, based on the view of the three imams.
This is an example of istiḥsān overriding qiyās.
3
Analyze the pledge ruling
For ʿinān partners, pledging partnership property for a personal debt is not valid; if done, detailed rules apply regarding liability. For mufāwaḍa partners, pledge and taking pledge on behalf of the partner is allowed.
The distinction between ʿinān and mufāwaḍa is key.
4
Note prohibitions on kitāba, marriage of slave-girl, and debt payment
These are not customary in trade and thus not allowed for a partner to do unilaterally.
Kitāba is a contract of gradual manumission, which is not a trade transaction.
5
Recognize the exception for the partner conducting sales
The one who conducts the sale may pledge for the price (thaman), as per al-Khāniyya.
This is a practical exception for the partner managing sales.

Commentary
This passage delineates the scope of a partner's authority in a partnership (both ʿinān and mufāwaḍa). The author opens by listing five actions a partner may undertake: bidaʿa (giving capital to another to trade with, keeping profit for the owner), hiring (istiʾjār, e.g., hiring an employee for trade or preservation), deposit (īdāʿ, safekeeping without charge), mudāraba (a form of profit-sharing partnership where the partner acts as investor, giving funds to an agent), and appointment of agents (tawkīl, delegating authority). Justifications are provided for each: bidaʿa is customary; hiring is common among merchants; deposit is permissible a fortiori since it is gratuitous; mudāraba is a lower level of partnership and thus is included; agency is essential for trade. There is a reported disagreement from Abū Ḥanīfa that a partner may not engage in mudāraba because it is itself a partnership, but the preferred view (based on the original transmission) allows it, since the aim is profit, not partnership per se. The author also notes that a partner may not form another partnership (mushāraka) without permission, unlike mudāraba. Apostile clarifies this restriction is not absolute, as the author will mention later. The passage then covers additional rulings not in the matn: lending (ʿāriyya) is disallowed by analogy, but istiḥsān exempts from liability; pledge (rahn) is prohibited for ʿinān partners without permission but allowed for mufāwaḍa partners; a partner cannot enter a kitāba contract, marry a slave-girl, or pay a debt unilaterally. Finally, if a partner takes funds as mudāraba, the profit is his.

Key Terms
عارية (ʿāriyya): Lending an item for free use, with the obligation to return it. In partnership context, lending partnership property without permission is restricted.
رهن (rahn): Pledge: giving an item as collateral for a debt. In partnership, rules differ for ʿinān and mufāwaḍa.
مكاتبة (mukātaba): A contract of manumission where a slave pays a sum over time in exchange for freedom. A partner may not enter such a contract with partnership funds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the supplementary rulings, which of the following is permitted for a partner in a mufāwaḍa partnership but not for an ʿinān partner?
A) Lending partnership property without permission
B) Pledging partnership property for a personal debt
C) Entering a kitāba contract
D) Marrying a slave-girl

Key Takeaway
Partners in ʿinān have limited authority to lend or pledge without permission; istiḥsān modifies qiyās in lending; mufāwaḍa partners have broader pledge authority.

Profit Distribution in a Partner's Mudaraba
Explains profit distribution when a partner takes mudaraba money from a third party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios of mudaraba profit distribution in a partnership and apply the ruling to each case.

Core Idea
Mudaraba profit belongs to the partner only if the trade is outside the partnership or done in presence; otherwise it is shared.

When one partner enters a mudaraba contract with a third party, the profit distribution depends on the nature of the trade and the partner's presence. The passage from al-Muhit provides a three-case ruling. Let's unpack each scenario and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the partner takes money as mudaraba from a third party. This is the key action being ruled upon.
2
Classify the trade
Determine whether the mudaraba transaction is within the scope of the partnership's trade or outside it.
The partnership's trade is the business activity agreed upon in the original partnership contract.
3
Check the partner's presence
Assess whether the partner who is not the mudarib was present or absent when the mudaraba money was taken.
4
Apply the three-case ruling
Based on the classification and presence, apply the ruling: (1) If the trade is outside the partnership, profit goes solely to the partner. (2) If the trade is within the partnership and the partner is present, profit also goes solely to the partner. (3) If the trade is within the partnership (or absolutely) and the partner is absent, profit is shared: half to the partner, half between the mudarib and the capital owner.
5
Understand the rationale
The partnership contract only covers the agreed trade; outside activities are personal to the partner. Presence matters because the absent partner is deemed to have consented or not opposed the action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاصة. أطلق الجواب في الكتاب وهو على التفصيل إن أخذ مالاً مضاربة ليتصرف فيما ليس من تجارتهما فالربح له خاصة لأنه لم يدخل تحت عقد الشركة، وكذلك إن أخذ المال مضاربة بحضرة صاحبه ليتصرف فيما هو من تجارتهما، وأما إذا أخذ المال مضاربة ليتصرف فيما كان من تجارتهما أو مطلقاً حال غيبة شريكه يكون الربح بينهما مشتركاً نصفه لشريكه ونصفه بين المضارب ورب المال؛ كذا في المحيط. فقوله في الكتاب يضارب معناه يدفع المال مضاربة، وأما أخذه المال مضاربة ففيه التفصيل كما علمت.
Specifically, the answer in the book is general but it is detailed: If he takes money as mudaraba to transact in something not of their trade, then the profit is exclusively his, because it did not enter under the partnership contract. Similarly, if he takes the money as mudaraba in the presence of his partner to transact in something that is of their trade. As for when he takes the money as mudaraba to transact in something that was of their trade, or absolutely, while his partner is absent, then the profit is shared between them: half for his partner, and half between the mudarib and the owner of the capital. This is in al-Muhit. So his statement in the book 'yudarib' means he gives the money as mudaraba. As for his taking money as mudaraba, there is the detail as you have learned.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on partnership. It addresses the scenario where one partner enters into a mudaraba contract with a third party using the partnership assets or his own? The author clarifies the ruling from al-Muhit. The key distinction is whether the mudaraba transaction falls within the scope of the partnership's trade. If the partner takes money as mudaraba for a business that is not part of the partnership's trade, then the profit belongs entirely to that partner because it is outside the partnership contract. If he does so in the presence of his partner for a trade within their partnership, the profit is also his alone? Wait: the text says 'also' for this case. The third case is when he takes the money for a trade within the partnership or absolutely while the partner is absent: then the profit is shared: half goes to the partner, and the other half is divided between the mudarib (the active partner) and the capital owner. This is a detailed ruling based on whether the partner is present and whether the trade is within the partnership scope.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudaraba): A contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit sharing as agreed.
شركة (sharika): Partnership; here specifically referring to the partnership between the two partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The profit is shared equally between the partners and the mudarib.
B) The profit belongs exclusively to the partner who took the mudaraba.
C) The profit belongs to the partnership.
D) The profit is invalid and must be given in charity.

Key Takeaway
The profit distribution in a partner's mudaraba depends on whether the trade is within the partnership scope and the partner's presence.

One Partner Deferring a Partnership Debt
Ruling on validity of one partner deferring a debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for each scenario of one partner deferring a partnership debt and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
A partner's authority to defer a partnership debt depends on whether he was the original contracting party.

When a partnership holds a debt, one partner may wish to grant an extension. But not all partners have equal authority. Al-Muhit presents three scenarios and the differing views of the early Hanafi masters. This lesson unpacks those positions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three scenarios: (1) the contracting partner defers, (2) the non-contracting partner defers, (3) both were parties and one defers.
The third scenario is treated like the second (non-contracting partner) in terms of ruling.
2
State each scholar's position for each scenario
For scenario 1: Sahibayn say valid for both shares without guarantee; Abu Yusuf says valid only in his share. For scenario 2 & 3: Abu Hanifa says not valid at all; Sahibayn say valid in his share.
Abu Hanifa's view on scenario 1 is not mentioned; likely he agrees with the majority.
3
Analyze the proof for the contracting partner's authority
The debt arises from a sale he made. Since he can cancel and resell with a deferred price, deferring is a lesser power (اولى). Thus he has authority without needing partner consent.
Contrast with an agent for sale: the agent who discharges a debt must guarantee it, but here no guarantee because the partner has greater autonomy.
4
Analyze the non-contracting partner's case
Abu Hanifa argues that a non-contracting partner lacks authority to alter contract terms. Sahibayn argue he owns a share of the debt, so he can defer his own portion.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, the deferment is void; under Sahibayn, it is valid for his share.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the non-contracting partner defers and the debtor pays later, under Sahibayn the deferring partner receives his share at the new date, while the other partner can demand his share immediately. Under Abu Hanifa, the deferment is ineffective and the debtor must pay both immediately.
This affects how the partnership and debtor should act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في المحيط : وإن كان لهما دين على آخر فأجله أحدهما فهو على ثلاثة أوجه : إن أجله العاقد جاز في النصيبين ولا يضمن نصيب شريكه عندهما وعند أبي يوسف يجوز في نصيبه ولا يجوز في نصيب شريكه. وأصله الوكيل بالبيع إذا أبرأ عن الثمن أو حط أو أجله عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف إلا أن هناك يضمن من ماله لموكله عندهما وهنا لا يضمن لأن العاقد هنا لو أقال العقد ثم باعه بنفسه ،جاز، فلما ملك إنشاء البيع بثمن إلى أجل فلأن يملك التأجيل فيه أولى. ولو أجل غير العاقد أو عقدا جميعاً فأجله أحدهما لم يجز عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يجوز في نصيبه.
He said in Al-Muhit: If they have a debt on someone, and one of them defers it, then it is on three aspects: If the contracting partner defers it, it is valid for both shares and he does not guarantee his partner's share according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, it is valid in his share and not valid in his partner's share. The origin is the agent for sale: if he grants a discharge from the price, or reduces it, or defers it, according to the two it is valid, contrary to Abu Yusuf, except that there he guarantees from his own wealth for his principal according to the two, but here he does not guarantee because the contracting partner, if he cancels the contract and then sells it himself, it is permissible. So when he has the power to initiate a sale with a deferred price, it is more appropriate that he has the power to defer. And if the non-contracting partner defers, or both contracted and one of them defers, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two it is permissible in his share.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding one partner deferring a debt that is jointly owed to the partnership. Al-Muhit presents three scenarios: (1) The partner who originally contracted the debt (the one who made the sale) defers it. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), this deferment is valid for both partners' shares, and the deferring partner does not guarantee his partner's share. Abu Yusuf alone holds that it is valid only in his own share. The analogy is made to an agent in a sale: if the agent discharges or reduces the price, the Sahibayn (but not Abu Yusuf) hold it valid, but the agent must compensate his principal. Here, no compensation is needed because the contracting partner has the power to cancel and resell. (2) If a non-contracting partner defers, or if both were parties to the contract but only one defers, then Abu Hanifa says it is not valid at all, while the Sahibayn say it is valid in his own share. This shows a difference in the authority of partners to unilaterally modify a contract.

Key Terms
تأجيل (ta'jil): Postponing the due date of a debt, granting an extension.
العاقد (al-'aqid): The partner who originally made the contract (sale) that created the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if the contracting partner defers a partnership debt, what is the ruling?
A) Valid only in his share and he guarantees his partner's share.
B) Valid in both shares and he does not guarantee.
C) Not valid at all.
D) Valid only if both partners agree.

Key Takeaway
The authority to defer a partnership debt depends on whether the partner was the original contracting party; the Sahibayn grant broader authority than Abu Hanifa or Abu Yusuf in certain scenarios.

Partner Lending Partnership Money: Zahir al-Riwaya vs. Istihsan
Ruling on whether a partner may lend partnership money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a partner lending partnership money in the zahir al-riwaya, explain the qiyas and istihsan reasoning, and distinguish between the two transmissions.

Core Idea
A partner cannot lend partnership money in the well-known position because it is a voluntary gift; istihsan allows it by analogy to ariya.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a subtle point in partnership law: may one partner unilaterally lend partnership funds to a third party? The ruling touches on authority, the nature of lending, and the interplay between qiyas and istihsan. Understanding this shows how Hanafi fiqh balances strict analogy with juristic preference.

Guided Path
1
State the zahir al-riwaya ruling
Identify the primary ruling: 'لا يملك الإقراض' – the partner does not have the right to lend partnership money, even in a mufawada partnership.
Zahir al-riwaya refers to the well-known transmitted rulings of Imam Muhammad in the six core books.
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
The text gives the reason: lending (iqrad) is akin to a loan for use (ariya) in legal effect and custom, and ariya is a voluntary gift (tabarru'). One partner cannot unilaterally make a gift of partnership property.
The analogy is based on the shared characteristic of being a non-compensatory transfer of benefit.
3
Recognize the istihsan exception
The author notes that ariya itself is prohibited by qiyas but permitted by istihsan. By extension, iqrad should also be permitted because it is either a type of ariya or an exchange (mu'awada) – both are acts within a partner's authority.
Istihsan here is based on custom and need, overriding strict qiyas.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Hasan ibn Ziyad transmitted that the partner does have the right to lend, relying on the istihsan reasoning. This is a nawadir transmission, not part of zahir al-riwaya.
The difference highlights the tension between strict analogy and pragmatic consideration.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Muhit states the zahir al-riwaya ruling (prohibition) as the relied-upon position. However, some later scholars may act on the istihsan view depending on circumstances.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwaya, but the istihsan remains a valid alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنه لا يملك الإقراض ولو مفاوضاً في ظاهر الرواية لأنه إعارة حكماً وعرفاً فهي تبرع فلا يملكه أحدهما كذا في المحيط. وقدمنا أن العارية ممنوعة قياساً جائزة استحساناً وهو يقتضي جواز الإقراض لأنه إما عارية وإما معاوضة وكل منهما يملكه أحدهما فلذا روى الحسن أنه يملك الإقراض
And among them: He does not have the right to lend, even if he is a mufawid (unlimited partner), in the zahir al-riwaya, because it is a lending (i'ara) in legal effect and custom, and it is a voluntary gift, so one of them does not have the right to do it, as stated in al-Muhit. And we have already stated that lending (ariya) is prohibited by qiyas but permissible by istihsan. And this implies the permissibility of lending (iqrad), because it is either ariya (loan of fungibles?) or mu'awada (exchange), and each of them is within the authority of one partner. Therefore, Hasan (ibn Ziyad) narrated that he does have the right to lend.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage deals with whether a partner in a partnership (even a mufawada partnership) may lend partnership money to a third party. In the zahir al-riwaya (the well-known transmitted rulings of Imam Muhammad), it is not permitted because lending is considered a voluntary transfer of ownership (tabarru') similar to a loan for use (ariya), which is a gift. As a gift, one partner doing it without the other's consent is not valid since it reduces the partnership assets. However, the author notes that previously they stated that ariya itself is prohibited by qiyas (analogy) but permitted by istihsan (juristic preference). Applying that logic, iqrad (lending fungibles) should also be permitted because it can be considered either a type of ariya (if the items are to be returned) or a kind of exchange (mu'awada) since the borrower returns its equivalent. Both ariya and mu'awada are acts that one partner can do (e.g., giving a loan for use or making a sale). Therefore, Hasan ibn Ziyad transmitted a position that the partner may lend. This shows a difference between the zahir al-riwaya and a nawadir transmission.

Key Terms
إقراض (iqrad): Lending money or fungibles with the obligation to return the equivalent.
عارية (ariya): Loan of a non-fungible item for use; here used as analogy for iqrad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason given in the zahir al-riwaya for prohibiting a partner from lending partnership money?
A) Because it is a form of riba.
B) Because it is an 'ariya (loan for use) in legal effect and custom, and it is a tabarru' (gift).
C) Because the partner does not have full ownership of the money.
D) Because it might lead to loss of the money.

Key Takeaway
A partner lacks authority to lend partnership money in the well-known Hanafi position because it is treated as a gift, but a valid transmission allows it by istihsan.

Ruling on a Partner Traveling with Partnership Money
Intra-Hanafi dispute on traveling with partnership capital

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi position on a partner traveling with partnership money and explain the reasoning that expenses are capital costs.

Core Idea
A partner may travel with partnership money because travel expenses are capital costs, not personal losses.

When partners pool capital for trade, questions arise about the scope of authority. One common issue is whether a partner can travel with the partnership funds without explicit permission. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) permits it, while Abu Yusuf restricts it. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the majority view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
The ruling covers the partner, the mustabda' (one who sends goods), the mudarib, and the depositary. Recognize that they all handle another's property.
The key is the ability to travel with the asset.
2
State the majority position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Sahibayn), these individuals have the right to travel with the money, regardless of whether they incur expenses.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
3
Identify the opposing view
Abu Yusuf disagrees: traveling without explicit permission is not allowed, implying liability for loss if such travel occurs.
His basis is that travel imposes additional risk beyond normal trading.
4
Analyze the majority's reasoning (talil)
The expenses incurred during travel are attached to the capital (mulhaq bi-ra's al-mal). Merchants do not consider them as losses (gharama) but as operational costs.
Thus, the traveling partner is not personally liable for those expenses.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the majority view, if the partner travels and the money is lost, he is not liable for the travel expenses (they are capital costs). Under Abu Yusuf, he would be liable for the entire loss because he acted outside his authority.
The practical difference is about liability for losses during travel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنه يملك السفر بالمال هو والمستبضع والمضارب والمودع عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف، سواء كان له حمل ومؤنة أو لا، لأن ما يلحقه من المؤنة فهو ملحق برأس المال ولا يعده التجار من باب الغرامة.
And among them: That he has the right to travel with the money, he and the one who sends goods for trade (mustabda'), the mudarib, and the depositary, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf, whether he has a load and expense or not, because the expense that befalls him is attached to the capital, and traders do not consider it from the category of loss.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a partner (and other agents like mustabda', mudarib, and depositary) may travel with the partnership or entrusted property. According to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: 'عندهما'), it is permissible even if it incurs expenses for transportation and lodging, because these expenses are considered part of the capital cost, not a loss. Abu Yusuf disagrees and does not permit it. The reasoning given is that the expenses incurred are attached to the capital (i.e., they are business expenses) and merchants do not consider them as losses (gharama) but rather as operational costs. This ruling applies even if there is no explicit permission to travel.

Key Terms
المستبضع (al-mustabda'): One who sends goods with another for trade; a type of agent.
مؤنة (mu'na): Expenses incurred, such as transportation and lodging.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, can a partner travel with partnership money without explicit permission?
A) No, because it involves additional risk.
B) Yes, because expenses are attached to capital.
C) Yes, but only if he bears the expenses personally.
D) No, unless the partner gives permission.

Key Takeaway
A partner may travel with partnership money; travel expenses are capital costs, not personal losses.
