When a Partner's Purchase is for Himself or the Partnership
Ruling on partner's purchase funding source

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish whether a partner's purchase binds the partnership or is for himself alone, and state the underlying rule.

Core Idea
A partner's purchase binds the partnership only if he uses partnership funds.

In a partnership, not every purchase by a partner automatically belongs to the partnership. The key factor is the source of funds: if he uses partnership money, the purchase is for the partnership; if he uses his own money or credit, the purchase is his alone unless authorized. This lesson clarifies the ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purchase scenario
Determine whether the partner had partnership money in his hand at the time of purchase.
The text says: 'إذا كان في يده مال الشركة فهو على الشركة' (if there is partnership money in his hand, it is on the partnership).
2
Check the funding source
If he buys with dirhams or dinars that are his own (not partnership funds), the purchase is for him alone.
The text explicitly says: 'فإن اشترى بدراهم أو دنانير فالشراء له خاصة' (if he buys with dirhams or dinars, the purchase is specifically for him).
3
Understand the reason
The ruling is based on the principle that a partner cannot incur debt for the partnership without explicit authority. Using his own money or credit does not obligate the partnership.
The text states: 'لأنه لو صار على الشركة مستديناً وأنه لا يملك ذلك' (because if it were on the partnership, he would become indebted, and he does not have the authority to do that).
4
Note the exception for authorization
If one partner authorizes the other to buy on credit, then the purchase may bind both, but the default is that the buyer alone is liable.
The text briefly mentions: 'وإن قال أحدهما للآخر جازت' (if one says to the other [you may act], it is permissible).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشركة
أن بالعقد والنسيئة وإن اشترى؛ إن كان في يده مال الشركة فهو على الشركة، وإن لم يبيع يكن، فإن اشترى بدراهم أو دنانير فالشراء له خاصة دون شريكه لأنه لو صار على الشركة مستديناً وأنه لا يملك ذلك، وإن قال أحدهما للآخر جازت، وإن باع أحدهما متاعا بع ورد عليه فقبله جاز ولو بلا قضاء، وكذا لو حط أو أخر من عيب، وإن بلا عيب جاز في وكذا لو وهب ولو أقر بعيب في متاع باعه جاز عليهما، ولو قال كل منهما للآخر حصته، اعمل برأيك فلكل منهما أن يعمل ما يقع في التجارة كالرهن والارتهان والسفر والخلط بماله والشركة بالغير لا الهبة والقرض وما كان إتلافاً للمال أو تمليكاً بغير عوض فإنه لا يجوز وإن قال له اعمل برأيك ما لم يصرح به نصاً. وإن أذن كل منهما للآخر بالاستقراض لا يرجع المقرض على الآخر لأن التوكيل به لا يصح ولو باع أحدهما لم يكن للآخر قبض الثمن، وكذا دين وليه أحدهما وللمديون أن يمتنع من الدفع إليه وإن دفع إلى الشريك برئ من نصيبه ولم يبرأ من حصة الدائن استحساناً، والقياس أن لا يبرأ من حصة القابض أيضاً المفاوض ممن لا تقبل شهادته له ينفذ على المفاوضة إجماعاً، أما الإقرار اهـ . ثم قال بعده : بيع بالدين لا ينفذ عنده . وفي الخانية : ليس لأحدهما أن يخاصم فيما باع صاحبه وقبض الذي باع وتوكيله جائز عليه وعلى شريكه. ولو وكل أحدهما رجلاً في بيع أو شرا راء وأخرجه الآخر عن الوكالة صار خارجاً عنها، فإن وكل البائع رجلاً بتقاضي ثمن ما باع ليس للآخر أن يخرجه عن الوكالة. ولو قال أحدهما لصاحبه اخرج إلى نيسابور ولا تجاوز فجاوز فهلك المال
ضمن حصة الشريك، ولو شارك أحد الشريكين رجلاً شركة عنان فما اشترى الشريك الثالث كان النصف للمشتري والنصف بين الشريكين الأولين وما اشتراه الشريك الذي لم يشارك فهو بينه وبين شريكه نصفين ولا شيء منه للشريك الثالث ولو استقرض أحد شريكي العنان مالاً للتجارة لزمهما لأنه تمليك مال بمال فكان بمنزلة الصرف ولو أقر أحد الشريكين أنه فلان ألفاً استقرض من من تجارتهما تلزمه خاصة .اهـ.
Book of Partnership. That [the partner's purchase] is with cash and credit. If he buys, if there is partnership money in his hand, it is on the partnership. If he does not have [money], then if he buys with dirhams or dinars, the purchase is specifically for him, not for his partner, because if it were on the partnership he would become indebted, and he does not have the right to do that. If one of them says to the other [you can act], it is permissible. If one of them sells merchandise and it is returned to him [due to defect] and he accepts, it is valid even without a court ruling. Likewise, if he reduces [the price] or postpones it due to a defect, and without a defect it is valid. Likewise, if he gives it as a gift. If he acknowledges a defect in merchandise he sold, it is binding on both. If each says to the other regarding his share: 'Act according to your opinion,' then each may do what is customary in trade, such as pawning, borrowing, traveling, mixing his own property, and partnership with a third party; but [they may] not [do] gifting, loaning, or anything that destroys property or gives ownership without compensation, even if he said 'act according to your opinion' unless he explicitly stated so. If each authorizes the other to borrow, the lender does not have recourse against the other partner because the agency for borrowing is not valid. If one of them sells, the other does not have the right to receive the price. Similarly, if a debt is owed to one of them, the debtor may refuse to pay the partner. If he pays the partner, he is discharged from the partner's share but not from the creditor's share, by istihsan. The qiyas would be that he is not discharged even from the share of the receiver. The mufawada partner from whom testimony is not accepted has authority over the mufawada by consensus. As for acknowledgment, etc. Then he said after that: selling on credit is not effective according to him. In al-Khaniya: One of them cannot litigate regarding what his partner sold, and the one who sold receives [the price], and his agency is valid against him and his partner. If one of them appoints a man to sell or buy and the other removes him from agency, he is removed. If the seller appoints a man to collect the price of what he sold, the other cannot remove him from agency. If one says to his companion: 'Go to Nishapur and do not exceed [that]' and he exceeded and the property was lost, it is within the partner's share [i.e., the transgressor is liable for his partner's share]. If one of the two partners enters into an 'inan partnership with a man, then what the third partner buys is half for the buyer and half between the first two partners. What the partner who did not enter the partnership buys is half between him and his partner, and nothing from it for the third partner. If one of the two 'inan partners borrows money for trade, it is binding on both because it is ownership of property for property, so it is like a currency exchange. If one of the two partners acknowledges that so-and-so borrowed a thousand from their business, it is binding on him alone.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the chapter of Partnership. It begins by explaining rulings on a partner's purchase. If a partner buys using partnership money in his possession, the purchase is for the partnership. If he buys with his own money (dirhams/dinars) without partnership funds, the purchase is for himself alone. The reason given is that if it were on the partnership, he would be incurring debt for the partnership without having the authority to do so. The author then discusses various scenarios: when one partner authorizes the other, when a sale is returned due to a defect, reduction or postponement of price, gifting the price, etc. A key principle: a partner who is given general authority ('act according to your opinion') may engage in customary trade transactions like pawning, borrowing, traveling, mixing funds, and forming sub-partnerships, but not gifting or lending gratuitously, as these are not trade. The passage also addresses borrowing: if one partner authorizes the other to borrow, the lender cannot sue the non-borrowing partner because agency for borrowing is not valid. Regarding payment of a debt to a partner: if a debtor pays a partner, he is discharged from the partner's share but not from the creditor's share (the other partner's share) by istihsan (juristic preference), contrary to qiyas which would not discharge him at all. The text then quotes al-Khaniya on matters of litigation, agency, and exceeding instructions. Finally, it covers scenarios involving a third partner in an 'inan partnership and borrowing for trade: a loan for trade binds both partners because it is an exchange of property for property, analogous to currency exchange. However, an acknowledgment of a debt from the business is binding only on the acknowledging partner.

Key Terms
شركة العنان (shirkat al-'inan): Partnership where partners contribute capital and trade, with limited liability.
دراهم (darahim): Silver dirhams, used as currency; here meaning personal money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a partner buys goods with his own dirhams (personal funds) in an 'inan partnership, the goods belong to:
A) The partnership
B) The buying partner alone
C) Both partners equally
D) The seller until payment

Key Takeaway
A partner's purchase belongs to the partnership only if made with partnership funds; otherwise it is his alone.

Scope of Partner's Authority: Permitted vs. Prohibited Acts
Ruling on scope of partner's authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list which acts a partner with general authority may perform and which are prohibited, and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
General authority covers trade but not gratuitous transfers or destruction of property.

When a partner says 'act according to your opinion', the partner is authorized to perform customary trade transactions. However, this does not extend to gifting, loaning, or destroying property. This lesson delineates the boundaries of a partner's authority in an 'inan partnership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authorization phrase
The text describes the case: 'wa in qala kull minhuma lilakhar hissatahu, i'mal bira'yik' (if each says to the other regarding his share: act according to your opinion).
This phrase is key to understanding broad authority.
2
List permissible acts
Permissible acts include: pawning (al-rahn), borrowing (al-irtihan), traveling (al-safar), mixing funds (al-khalt bimilih), and forming partnerships with third parties (al-shirkah bilghayr).
These are considered 'ma yaqa' fi al-tijarah' (what occurs in trade).
3
List prohibited acts
Prohibited acts even with general authority: giving gifts (al-hiba), lending without interest (al-qard), and anything that destroys wealth (itlaf) or gives ownership without compensation (tamlik bighayr 'iwad).
The text says: 'la al-hibah wa al-qard wa ma kan itlafan lilmal aw tamlikan bighayr 'iwad'.
4
Understand the rationale
Trade aims at profit; gratuitous transfers defeat that purpose. Destroying wealth is contrary to the partnership's objective.
The authority is limited to acts that generate profit or preserve capital.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشركة
أن بالعقد والنسيئة وإن اشترى؛ إن كان في يده مال الشركة فهو على الشركة، وإن لم يبيع يكن، فإن اشترى بدراهم أو دنانير فالشراء له خاصة دون شريكه لأنه لو صار على الشركة مستديناً وأنه لا يملك ذلك، وإن قال أحدهما للآخر جازت، وإن باع أحدهما متاعا بع ورد عليه فقبله جاز ولو بلا قضاء، وكذا لو حط أو أخر من عيب، وإن بلا عيب جاز في وكذا لو وهب ولو أقر بعيب في متاع باعه جاز عليهما، ولو قال كل منهما للآخر حصته، اعمل برأيك فلكل منهما أن يعمل ما يقع في التجارة كالرهن والارتهان والسفر والخلط بماله والشركة بالغير لا الهبة والقرض وما كان إتلافاً للمال أو تمليكاً بغير عوض فإنه لا يجوز وإن قال له اعمل برأيك ما لم يصرح به نصاً. وإن أذن كل منهما للآخر بالاستقراض لا يرجع المقرض على الآخر لأن التوكيل به لا يصح ولو باع أحدهما لم يكن للآخر قبض الثمن، وكذا دين وليه أحدهما وللمديون أن يمتنع من الدفع إليه وإن دفع إلى الشريك برئ من نصيبه ولم يبرأ من حصة الدائن استحساناً، والقياس أن لا يبرأ من حصة القابض أيضاً المفاوض ممن لا تقبل شهادته له ينفذ على المفاوضة إجماعاً، أما الإقرار اهـ . ثم قال بعده : بيع بالدين لا ينفذ عنده . وفي الخانية : ليس لأحدهما أن يخاصم فيما باع صاحبه وقبض الذي باع وتوكيله جائز عليه وعلى شريكه. ولو وكل أحدهما رجلاً في بيع أو شرا راء وأخرجه الآخر عن الوكالة صار خارجاً عنها، فإن وكل البائع رجلاً بتقاضي ثمن ما باع ليس للآخر أن يخرجه عن الوكالة. ولو قال أحدهما لصاحبه اخرج إلى نيسابور ولا تجاوز فجاوز فهلك المال
ضمن حصة الشريك، ولو شارك أحد الشريكين رجلاً شركة عنان فما اشترى الشريك الثالث كان النصف للمشتري والنصف بين الشريكين الأولين وما اشتراه الشريك الذي لم يشارك فهو بينه وبين شريكه نصفين ولا شيء منه للشريك الثالث ولو استقرض أحد شريكي العنان مالاً للتجارة لزمهما لأنه تمليك مال بمال فكان بمنزلة الصرف ولو أقر أحد الشريكين أنه فلان ألفاً استقرض من من تجارتهما تلزمه خاصة .اهـ.

Payment to a Partner: The Role of Istihsan
Ruler on payment discharge via istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that paying a partner discharges the debtor from the partner's share only, and contrast qiyas with istihsan.

Core Idea
By istihsan, paying a partner clears the payer from that partner's share, protecting good-faith debtors.

When a debtor pays a debt owed to the partnership to one partner, does he become fully discharged? The strict qiyas says no, because the partner is not a valid agent for collecting the other partner's share. However, Hanafi jurists apply istihsan (juristic preference) to partially discharge the debtor, balancing legal precision with practical fairness.

Guided Path
1
Present the scenario
One partner is owed a debt (say, from a customer). The debtor pays the amount to the other partner (not the creditor partner).
The text says: 'wa law dafa'a ila al-shariki bari'a min nasibihi wa lam yabra' min hissat al-da'in' (if he pays the partner, he is discharged from his share but not from the share of the creditor).
2
State the qiyas ruling
Under strict analogy (qiyas), the debtor is not discharged at all, because the partner receiving payment has no authority to collect for the other partner. The text says: 'wal-qiyas an la yabra'a min hissat al-qabidh aydan' (the qiyas is that he is not discharged even from the share of the receiver).
So qiyas says the debtor remains liable to both partners.
3
State the istihsan ruling
By istihsan, the debtor is discharged from the share of the partner who received payment, but not from the share of the other partner. The receiving partner is treated as having authority over his own share.
The text says: 'istihsan'an' (by istihsan).
4
Understand the rationale for istihsan
Istihsan is applied to facilitate transactions and protect debtors who pay in good faith to a partner who appears authorized to receive payment for the partnership.
The text implies this by saying 'istihsan' without a specific proof, relying on the need for ease in trade.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside strict analogy for a more equitable ruling.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning, a source of Islamic law.

A) Fully discharged

The Mufawada Partner's Gift or Absolution of the Price: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Dispute on hiba/ibra by a mufawada partner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a mufawada partner's hiba or ibra of the price and identify the practical difference between the views of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A mufawada partner may forgive the price, but he must guarantee his partner's share.

In mufawada partnership, partners have broad authority. But can one partner unilaterally gift away the price from a sale? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq records a famous intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding this ruling is crucial for partnership transactions and clarifies the limits of partner authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
The scenario: a mufawada partner sells partnership goods and then gifts the price to the buyer or absolves him from payment. The dispute is between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad (valid) and Abu Yusuf (invalid).
Note that this is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, meaning both views are within the school.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the gift/ibra is valid, but the selling partner must guarantee his partner's share (yadman nasib sahibihi).
The guarantee compensates the co-partner for the loss of his share.
3
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf does not permit the gift or ibra at all, presumably because he views it as an unauthorized disposition of the other partner's property without proper compensation.
His reasoning is not given in the text, but it is based on the idea that such unilateral forgiveness is akin to destruction (itlaf).
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the majority view, the transaction stands but the forgiving partner owes his partner the share; under Abu Yusuf, the transaction is invalid and the buyer must still pay.
This affects whether the buyer can keep the goods without paying.
5
Note the consensus rule for non-selling partners
If a partner other than the seller offers the gift, it is valid only for his own share by consensus, as he has no authority over the other's share without compensation.
This clarifies that the dispute is specifically about the selling partner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : إذا باع أحد المتفاوضين شيئاً من تجارتهما ثم إن البائع وهب الثمن من المشتري أو أبرأه منه جاز في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف، ولو وهب غير البائع جاز في حصته فقط إجماعاً.
قوله : (ويده في المال (أمانة أي الشريك لأنه قبض المال بإذن المالك لا على وجه البدل والوثيقة فصار كالوديعة ؛ كذا في الهداية. وخرج بالأول المقبوض على سوم الشراء، وبالثاني الرهن كما في النهاية : وظاهر كلامهم هنا أنه لو ادعى دفع المال إلى شريكه فالقول له مع اليمين، سواء كان في حياته أو بعد موته وظاهر كلام الولوالجي في الوكالة يفيده فإنه قال :
قوله : (ولو استقرض أحد شريكي العنان مالا (الخ) لا ينافي ما مر قريباً من أنه لو أذن كل منهما للآخر بالاستقراض لا يرجع المقرض على الآخر لأنه لا يلزم من كون ما استقرضه أحدهما يلزمها أن يرجع المقرض على الآخر، نظيره ما لو اشترى شيئاً طولب المشتري فقط كما مر . قوله : (ولو أقر الخ) قال في جواهر الفتاوى من أول باب الشركة : تصرف أحد الشريكين في البلد والآخر في السفر فلما أراد القسمة قال الذي في يده المال قد استقرضت مائة دينار وآخذ عوضها؛ إن كان المال في يد المقر فالإقرار صحيح وله أن يأخذ المائة .اهـ. وبمثله أفتى العلامة خير الدين. وقال في حاشيته على المنح ما نصه : أقول ووجه ذلك أنه إذا كان المال في يده وقد تقرر أنه أمين فقد ادعى أن مائة دينار منها حق الغير بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن في يده لأنه يدعي ديناً عليه فلا يقبل. وأقول : لو قال لي في هذا المال الذي في يدي كذا يقبل أيضاً لأنه ذو اليد والقول قول ذي اليد فيما بيده أنه له كما يقبل قوله أنه للغير تأمل وهي واقعة الفتوى وبه أفتيت اهـ كلامه لكن يرد على ما في الجواهر عبارة الخانية ويمكن الجواب بحمل ما في الخانية على ما إذا لم يكن المال في يده، وما في الجواهر على ما إذا كان في يده كما يستفاد من عبارة ،الجواهر وتعليل الشيخ خير الدين والمطلق يحمل على المقيد إذا اتحدت الحادثة والحكم كذا في المجموعة الصغيرة بخط ملا علي التركماني أمين الفتوى بدمشق رحمه الله تعالى قوله : (وفي الظهيرية إذا باع أحد المتفاوضين شيئاً الخ) انظره مع ما مر عن البزازية من قوله «وما كان إتلافاً للمال أو تمليكاً بغير عوض فإنه لا يجوز ثم راجعت الظهيرية فرأيته قال : ويضمن نصيب صاحبه بعد قوله جاز في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وكذا قال في الخانية كما قدمناه عنها. قوله: (وظاهر كلام الولوالجي (الخ) قال الرملي : ليست هذه عبارته وإنما عبارته: ولو وكل بقبض وديعة ثم مات الموكل فقال الوكيل قبضت في حياته وهلك وأنكرت الورثة، أو قال دفعته إليه صدق ولو كان ديناً لم يصدق لأن الوكيل في الموضعين حكى أمراً لا يملك استئنافه لكن
In al-Zahiriyya: If one of the two mufawada partners sells something from their business, then the seller gives the price to the buyer as a gift or absolves him from it, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. If someone other than the seller gives a gift, it is valid only for his share by consensus.
His statement: 'And his hand over the property is a trust,' meaning the partner's, because he took the property with the owner's permission, not as a substitute or security, so it becomes like a deposit. Thus in al-Hidaya. By the first [condition] is excluded what is taken with intent to purchase, by the second is excluded pawn, as in al-Nihaya. It appears from their statements that if he claims to have given the property to his partner, his word is accepted with an oath, whether during his lifetime or after his death. The apparent statement of al-Walwalji in the chapter on agency indicates this, for he said:
His statement: 'And if one of the two 'inan partners borrows money (etc.)' does not contradict what came earlier that if each authorized the other to borrow, the lender does not have recourse against the other, because it does not follow from the fact that what one borrowed binds them that the lender has recourse against the other. Its analogy is that if he bought something, only the buyer is sued, as before. His statement: 'And if he acknowledges (etc.)' He said in Jawahir al-Fatawa from the beginning of the chapter on Partnership: One of the two partners transacted in the city and the other in travel, and when he wanted to divide, the one who had the property in his hand said: 'I borrowed a hundred dinars and I will take its substitute.' If the property is in the hand of the one making the acknowledgment, the acknowledgment is valid and he may take the hundred. End quote. The scholar Khayr al-Din gave a similar fatwa. He said in his gloss on al-Minh: I say: The reason is that when the property is in his hand and it has been established that he is a trustee, he has claimed that a hundred dinars of it is the right of another, unlike when it is not in his hand, because then he is claiming a debt against himself, so it is not accepted. And I say: If he said: 'I have such-and-such in this property that is in my hand,' it is also accepted because he is the possessor and the word of the possessor regarding what is in his hand is accepted as it is his, just as his statement that it is for another is accepted. Reflect. This is the case of the fatwa and I gave a fatwa with it. End quote. But the statement of al-Khaniya contradicts what is in Jawahir, and it can be answered by interpreting al-Khaniya as when the property is not in his hand, and Jawahir as when it is in his hand, as understood from Jawahir's wording and the reasoning of Shaykh Khayr al-Din. The absolute is carried on the restricted when the incident and ruling are the same. Thus in al-Majmu'a al-Saghira by the hand of Mawla Ali al-Turkumani, the mufti of Damascus, may Allah have mercy on him. His statement: 'And in al-Zahiriyya, if one of the two mufawada partners sells something (etc.)' Look at it along with what came earlier from al-Bazzaziyya: 'And whatever is destruction of property or giving ownership without compensation is not valid.' Then I checked al-Zahiriyya and saw that he said: 'And he guarantees the share of his partner' after his statement 'it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.' Likewise said in al-Khaniya as we quoted earlier from her. His statement: 'And the apparent statement of al-Walwalji (etc.)' Al-Ramli said: This is not his wording; rather his wording is: If he appointed an agent to receive a deposit, then the principal died, and the agent said 'I received it during his lifetime and it perished' and the heirs denied, or he said 'I gave it to him,' he is believed. But if it was a debt, he would not be believed because the agent in both cases reported something that he cannot initiate afresh.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on partnership with a significant intra-Hanafi dispute. The text quotes al-Zahiriyya regarding a mufawada partnership: if one partner sells partnership goods and then gifts the price to the buyer or absolves him from payment, this is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf. However, if a non-selling partner does the same, it is valid only for his share by consensus. The author explains that the selling partner must guarantee his partner's share, as stated in al-Zahiriyya: 'he guarantees the share of his partner.' This is consistent with al-Khaniya. The author then comments on the principle that a partner's hand over the partnership property is a trust (amanah), like a deposit. This means that if a partner claims to have given the property to his co-partner, his word is accepted with an oath. The passage then addresses apparent contradictions: a loan taken by one 'inan partner for trade binds both partners, but earlier it was said that if each authorizes the other to borrow, the lender cannot sue the other. The author resolves this by noting that binding the partnership internally does not mean the lender has direct recourse. Similarly, regarding acknowledgment of a debt from the business, the text from Jawahir al-Fatawa states that if the partner acknowledges while the property is in his hand, it is valid; otherwise not. This is reconciled with al-Khaniya by distinguishing whether the property is in the acknowledging partner's hand. The passage concludes with a note from al-Ramli correcting the attribution of a statement to al-Walwalji.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Absolution or release from a debt; here referring to the seller absolving the buyer from paying the price.
أمانة (amanah): Trust; the partner's possession of partnership funds is a trust, not a guarantee (like a deposit), so he is not liable for loss without negligence.
مفاوض (mufawid): A partner in a mufawada partnership, which is a full partnership with equal authority and liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what is the consequence when a mufawada partner gifts the price to the buyer?
A) The gift is invalid; the buyer must still pay.
B) The gift is valid and the partner owes nothing.
C) The gift is valid but the partner must guarantee his co-partner's share.
D) The gift is valid only if the co-partner agrees.

Key Takeaway
In mufawada partnership, a selling partner may forgive the price but must compensate his partner, while a non-selling partner's forgiveness only affects his own share.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
8 min
The Partner's Hand as a Trust: Legal Implications for Claims and Acknowledgments
Definition and implications of partner's hand as amanah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a partner's possession is a trust (amanah) to determine the evidentiary weight of a partner's claim regarding partnership property.

Core Idea
A partner's hand over partnership assets is a trust – his word is accepted concerning what is in his possession.

Partners often hold partnership property. Is their possession a guarantee or a trust? The commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes that a partner's hand is a trust (amanah), like a deposit. This principle has critical implications: if a partner claims to have given property to a co-partner, his word is accepted with an oath. This lesson explores the definition of amanah in this context and its applications to loans and acknowledgments.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of amanah for a partner's possession
The partner took the property with the owner's permission, not as a substitute (like in a sale) or as security (like a pledge). Therefore, it is a trust, similar to a deposit (wadi'ah).
This distinguishes it from possession on approval (sawm al-shira) or pledge (rahn).
2
Understand the evidentiary implication
Because the partner is a trustee, if he claims to have delivered the property to his co-partner, his word is accepted with an oath – both during his lifetime and after death.
This is similar to the rule for any trustee (amin).
3
Apply to a loan scenario
If one of two 'inan partners borrows money for the partnership, the loan binds the partnership internally, but the lender does not have recourse against the other partner directly.
This reconciles the internal partnership liability with external creditor rights.
4
Apply to acknowledgment (iqrar)
If a partner acknowledges that he owes a debt from the partnership, the acknowledgment is valid only if the property is in his hand. If not, it is not accepted because he is claiming a debt against himself without possession.
The distinction: possession gives credibility to the claim.
5
Reconcile apparent contradictions
The text reconciles between al-Khaniya and Jawahir al-Fatawa by interpreting al-Khaniya as referring to when property is not in the partner's hand, and Jawahir as when it is in hand.
The principle: the absolute is carried on the restricted when the incident and ruling are the same.

Source Text

سوم الشراء (sawm al-shira): Taking goods on approval with intent to purchase; such possession is a guarantee (daman), not a trust.

Trustee's Claim After Death: Negation vs Imposition of Liability
Ruling with proof: distinction based on liability effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when a trustee's claim of payment/delivery after death is accepted based on whether it negates his own liability or imposes liability on the deceased.

Core Idea
A trustee's posthumous claim is accepted if it negates his own liability, but rejected if it imposes liability on the deceased.

This lesson explores a critical procedural rule in Hanafi fiqh: whose statement is believed when a trustee claims to have returned property after the owner's death? The answer hinges on whether the claim shifts liability away from the trustee or onto the deceased. We will examine the textual basis and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Trustee Type
Determine what kind of trustee the claimant is: agent for deposit, agent for debt, mudarib, partner, etc. Each has a different baseline liability.
The key is whether the trust property was in his hands as an amanah or as a collected debt.
2
Analyze the Direction of Liability
Ask: Does the claim negate the trustee's own liability (e.g., 'I returned the deposit') or does it impose liability on the deceased (e.g., 'I paid the debt to the principal')?
Negating liability = trustee was responsible; imposing liability = the deceased becomes responsible.
3
Apply the Rule
If the claim negates the trustee's liability, his statement is accepted (with oath). If it imposes liability on the deceased, his statement is rejected and proof is required.
This rule applies even after the owner's death; heirs step into his shoes.
4
Consider the Exception: Transgression
If the trustee exceeded his authority (ta'addi), he loses his trust status and becomes a guarantor (damin). His claim is no longer automatically accepted.
Transformation from amin to damin is a key Hanafi principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا ادعى الأمين بعد الموت الدفع في الحياة وأنكر الوارث فإن كان المقصود نفي الضمان عن نفسه كالوكيل بقبض الوديعة فالقول قوله وإن كان المقصود إيجاب الضمان على الميت كالوكيل بقبض الدين لا يقبل قوله .اهـ. وفي البزازية من باب التحليف : ولو ادعى المضارب أو الشريك دفع المال وأنكره رب المال يحلف المضارب أو الشريك الذي كان في يده المال اهـ. ولا يخفى أنه إذا تعدى صار ضامناً لأنه حكم الأمانات
If the trustee claims after death that he made payment during the lifetime, and the heir denies, then if the purpose is to negate liability from himself, like an agent for receiving a deposit, his statement is accepted. If the purpose is to impose liability on the deceased, like an agent for receiving a debt, his statement is not accepted. In al-Bazzaziyyah, from the chapter on administering oaths: If the mudarib or partner claims payment of the capital and the owner of the capital denies it, the mudarib or partner who had the capital in his hand takes an oath. It is not hidden that if he transgresses, he becomes a guarantor, because that is the ruling of trusts.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal principle of whose statement is believed regarding claims of payment or delivery of trust property after the death of the principal or in a partnership. The first part, from an earlier source, distinguishes between two scenarios: an agent for receiving a deposit (al-wakil bi qabd al-wadi'ah) claims after the principal's death that he paid the deposit back during the principal's lifetime. Since this claim negates his own liability (he was originally responsible for the deposit), he is believed, and the heirs cannot hold him liable. In contrast, an agent for receiving a debt (al-wakil bi qabd al-dayn) claims that he paid the collected debt to the principal. This claim would impose liability on the deceased principal (the debt was owed to the principal, so claiming payment to him makes the principal liable for that amount). Since this imposes liability on the deceased's estate, the agent is not believed; the heirs can demand proof. The next part from al-Bazzaziyyah deals with a similar situation in partnership: if a mudarib or partner claims he returned the capital to the owner, and the owner denies, the trustee (mudarib/partner) is believed upon oath. This is because his claim negates his own liability. The final comment states the general rule: if the trustee exceeds his authority (transgresses), he becomes a guarantor (damin) because the trust status is lost. The underlying rationale is that the trust (amanah) is based on integrity, and transgression converts it into a guarantee.

Key Terms
الأمين (al-amin): The trustee who holds property of another, such as an agent, partner, or mudarib.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability or guarantee; here, being responsible for the value of the property if lost after transgression.
الوكيل بقبض الوديعة (al-wakil bi qabd al-wadi'ah): An agent authorized to receive a deposit on behalf of the depositor.
الوكيل بقبض الدين (al-wakil bi qabd al-dayn): An agent authorized to collect a debt owed to the principal.
المضارب (al-mudarib): The working partner in a mudarabah (silent partnership) who manages the capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An agent for receiving a debt (wakil bi qabd al-dayn) claims after the principal's death that he paid the collected debt to the principal. The principal's heirs deny. Whose statement is accepted?
A) The agent's statement is accepted because he is a trustee.
B) The heirs' statement is accepted because the claim imposes liability on the deceased.
C) Both are believed equally.
D) The matter is referred to a judge to decide.

Key Takeaway
A trustee's posthumous claim is accepted only if it removes liability from himself, not if it places liability on the deceased's estate.

Validity of Restrictions in Partnership and Consequences of Violation
Covers validity of restricting partners to a place or cash and consequences of violation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on restrictions in partnership and determine the liability consequences when a partner violates a restriction.

Core Idea
A partner's restriction to a place or payment is valid; violation makes the partner liable for the other's share.

In Hanafi partnership law, partners may agree to specific limitations on where and how trade occurs. This lesson examines the ruling on restrictions to a particular place or to cash-only transactions, and the legal consequences when a partner exceeds those limitations, referencing fatwas from al-Bazzaziyyah and the author's own rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the restriction type
Determine if the restriction is to a place (e.g., Khwarazm) or to a payment method (e.g., cash only).
2
State the validity rule
Both types of restrictions are valid and binding in Hanafi law.
3
Apply the consequence of violation
Violating a place restriction makes the partner a guarantor of the other's share; violating a payment restriction may make the partner a usurper (ghasib) if removal is involved.
4
Analyze the fatwa scenarios
Examine the two fatwas: (1) selling on credit after being forbidden — sale binding on own share, suspended in partner's share; (2) removing goods after being forbidden — usurper status, profit not according to condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في البزازية : التقييد بالمكان صحيح حتى لو قال أحد الشريكين لصاحبه اخرج إلى خوارزم ولا تتجاوز عنه صح فلو جاوز عنه ضمن حصة شريكه. والتقييد بالنقد صحيح حتى لو قال لاتبع بالنسيئة صح، ولو اشتركا عناناً على أن يبيعا بالنقد والنسيئة ثم نهى أحدهما صاحبه عن البيع نسيئة وقد وقعت حادثتان أفتيت فيهما : الأولى نهاه عن البيع نسيئة فباع فأفتيت بنفاذه في حصته وبتوقفه في حصة شريكه، فإن أجاز قسم الربح بينهما . الثانية نهاه عن الإخراج فخرج ثم فأجبت بأنه غاصب حصة شريكه بالإخراج فينبغي أن لا يكون الربح على الشرط، ولم أر فيهما إلا ما قدمناه واعلم أنه ذكر الناطفي أن الأمانات تنقلب مضمونة بالموت عن تجهيل إلا في ثلاث : أحدها متولي المسجد إذا أخذ من غلات المسجد ومات من غير بيان لا يكون ضامناً. والثانية السلطان إذا خرج إلى الغزو وغنموا وأودع بعض الغنيمة عند بعض الغانمين ومات ولم يبين عند من أودع لا ضمان عليه والثالثة القاضي إذا أخذ مال اليتيم وأودع غيره ومات ولم يبين عند من أودع لا ضمان عليه. وأما أحد المتفاوضين إذا كان المال عنده ولم يبين حال المال الذي كان عنده ؛ ذكر بعض الفقهاء أنه لا يضمن وأحاله إلى شركة الأصل وذلك غلط، بل الصحيح أنه يضمن نصيب صاحبه ؛ كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان من كتاب الوقف . وبه تبين أن ما في فتح القدير وبعض الفتاوى ضعيف وأن الشريك ضامن بالموت عن تجهيل عناناً أو مفاوضة
He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: Restriction to a place is valid, so that if one of the partners says to his companion, 'Go out to Khwarazm and do not exceed it,' it is valid. If he exceeds it, he guarantees his partner's share. Restriction to cash is valid, so that if he says, 'Do not sell on credit,' it is valid. If they entered into an 'inan partnership agreeing to sell for cash and credit, then one forbade the other from selling on credit, and two incidents occurred for which I gave fatwas: First: He forbade him from selling on credit, but he sold. I gave a fatwa that it is binding in his own share and suspended in his partner's share; if the partner ratifies, the profit is divided between them. Second: He forbade him from removal, but he removed. I answered that he is a usurper of his partner's share by removal, so profit should not be according to the condition. I have not seen in them except what we have presented. Know that al-Natafi mentioned that trusts become guaranteed by death without clarification except in three: One: the custodian of the mosque, if he takes from the revenues of the mosque and dies without specifying, he is not a guarantor. Second: the sultan, if he goes out to war and they gain spoils, and he deposits some of the spoils with some of the warriors and dies without specifying with whom he deposited, there is no liability upon him. Third: the judge, if he takes the property of an orphan and deposits it with someone else and dies without specifying with whom he deposited, there is no liability upon him. As for one of the two partners in a mufawada, if the capital is with him and he does not clarify the state of the capital that was with him, some jurists mentioned that he does not guarantee and referred it to the original partnership, but that is a mistake. Rather, the correct view is that he guarantees his partner's share. This is in the Fatawa of Qadikhan from the book of Waqf. And by this it becomes clear that what is in Fath al-Qadir and some fatwas is weak, and that the partner is a guarantor by death without clarification, whether in an 'inan or mufawada partnership.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage covers several related rulings. First, restrictions in partnership: if a partner restricts the other to a specific place (e.g., Khwarazm) or to cash only (no credit), the restriction is valid. Violating it makes the violator liable for the other partner's share. The author relates two fatwas of his own: (1) if a partner sells on credit after being forbidden, the sale is binding on his own share but suspended regarding the other's share; if the other ratifies, they share profit. (2) if a partner removes goods after being forbidden from removal, he becomes a usurper of the other's share, so profit distribution should not follow the original condition. Next, a general rule from al-Natafi: trusts (amanat) become guaranteed upon death if the trustee dies without clarifying the property, with three exceptions: (a) the custodian of a mosque (mutawalli al-masjid) who takes from mosque revenues and dies without specifying—no liability; (b) a sultan who goes to war, deposits spoils with someone, and dies without specifying the depositary—no liability; (c) a judge who takes orphan property and deposits it without specifying—no liability. These exceptions are because their positions involve general public trust. However, for a partner in a mufawada (full mutual partnership), if he dies without clarifying the partnership capital in his possession, he is liable for his partner's share. Some earlier jurists incorrectly said he is not liable, but the correct view is from Fatawa Qadikhan: he guarantees. The author explicitly rejects the contrary view found in Fath al-Qadir and some fatwas, affirming the liability in both 'inan and mufawada partnerships.

Key Terms
التقييد بالمكان (al-taqyid bi al-makan): A condition in a partnership specifying a particular place where the partner may trade.
النسيئة (al-nasi'ah): Sale on credit, deferred payment.
الغاصب (al-ghasib): A usurper who wrongfully takes property; here, the partner who removes goods against the condition is considered a usurper of the other's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's fatwa, if a partner sells on credit after being forbidden, what is the status of the sale regarding the partner's own share?
A) The sale is void.
B) The sale is binding on his own share.
C) The sale is suspended.
D) The sale is valid only if the other partner ratifies.

Key Takeaway
A partner must adhere to agreed restrictions; violation creates liability for the other partner's share.

Trusts Becoming Guaranteed upon Death: Exceptions and the Mufawada Partner Dispute
Covers the rule of trusts becoming guaranteed upon death, three exceptions, and the mufawada partner dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three exceptions to the rule that trusts become guaranteed upon death without clarification, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a mufawada partner's liability.

Core Idea
A trustee is liable upon death without clarification, except for mosque custodians, sultans' agents, and judges; a mufawada partner is liable despite some jurists' contrary view.

A general Hanafi principle holds that trusts become guaranteed when the trustee dies without clarifying the property. However, al-Natafi identified three exceptions involving public trustees. This lesson also resolves a key intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a partner in a mufawada partnership is liable, siding with Fatawa Qadikhan over Fath al-Qadir.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Trusts (amānāt) become guaranteed (maḍmūnah) upon the trustee's death if the trustee does not clarify the property.
2
Memorize the three exceptions
The three exceptions are: (1) the custodian of a mosque (mutawallī al-masjid), (2) the sultan (or his agent) who deposits spoils of war, (3) the judge (qāḍī) who deposits an orphan's property.
These are public trustees acting in a general capacity.
3
Understand the rationale
Imposing liability on these public trustees would cause hardship and discourage public service; they are not considered ordinary trustees.
4
Identify the dispute
Some Hanafi jurists (referenced in Fatḥ al-Qadīr) held that a partner in a mufawada partnership is not liable upon death without clarification, analogizing to the original partnership.
5
Apply the tarjih
The author follows Fatawa Qadikhan, affirming that both 'inan and mufawada partners are liable upon death without clarification, rejecting the contrary view as a mistake.
The correct view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في البزازية : التقييد بالمكان صحيح حتى لو قال أحد الشريكين لصاحبه اخرج إلى خوارزم ولا تتجاوز عنه صح فلو جاوز عنه ضمن حصة شريكه. والتقييد بالنقد صحيح حتى لو قال لاتبع بالنسيئة صح، ولو اشتركا عناناً على أن يبيعا بالنقد والنسيئة ثم نهى أحدهما صاحبه عن البيع نسيئة وقد وقعت حادثتان أفتيت فيهما : الأولى نهاه عن البيع نسيئة فباع فأفتيت بنفاذه في حصته وبتوقفه في حصة شريكه، فإن أجاز قسم الربح بينهما . الثانية نهاه عن الإخراج فخرج ثم فأجبت بأنه غاصب حصة شريكه بالإخراج فينبغي أن لا يكون الربح على الشرط، ولم أر فيهما إلا ما قدمناه واعلم أنه ذكر الناطفي أن الأمانات تنقلب مضمونة بالموت عن تجهيل إلا في ثلاث : أحدها متولي المسجد إذا أخذ من غلات المسجد ومات من غير بيان لا يكون ضامناً. والثانية السلطان إذا خرج إلى الغزو وغنموا وأودع بعض الغنيمة عند بعض الغانمين ومات ولم يبين عند من أودع لا ضمان عليه والثالثة القاضي إذا أخذ مال اليتيم وأودع غيره ومات ولم يبين عند من أودع لا ضمان عليه. وأما أحد المتفاوضين إذا كان المال عنده ولم يبين حال المال الذي كان عنده ؛ ذكر بعض الفقهاء أنه لا يضمن وأحاله إلى شركة الأصل وذلك غلط، بل الصحيح أنه يضمن نصيب صاحبه ؛ كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان من كتاب الوقف . وبه تبين أن ما في فتح القدير وبعض الفتاوى ضعيف وأن الشريك ضامن بالموت عن تجهيل عناناً أو مفاوضة
He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: Restriction to a place is valid, so that if one of the partners says to his companion, 'Go out to Khwarazm and do not exceed it,' it is valid. If he exceeds it, he guarantees his partner's share. Restriction to cash is valid, so that if he says, 'Do not sell on credit,' it is valid. If they entered into an 'inan partnership agreeing to sell for cash and credit, then one forbade the other from selling on credit, and two incidents occurred for which I gave fatwas: First: He forbade him from selling on credit, but he sold. Key Terms
الأمانات تنقلب مضمونة (al-amanat tanqalib madmunah): Trusts become guaranteed (liable) upon death without clarification, except in three cases.
المتفاوضين (al-mutafawidayn): The two partners in a mufawada (full mutual partnership), where each is agent and surety for the other in all dealings.
متولي المسجد (mutawalli al-masjid): The custodian or manager of a mosque who oversees its revenues and expenses.
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or sovereign; in this context, the sultan who leads a military expedition and deposits spoils.
القاضي (al-qadi): The judge, who may take an orphan's property and deposit it with a third party.

Key Takeaway

The Validity and Scope of Shirkat al-Sana'i'
Explains the validity and conditions of shirkat al-sana'i'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid partnership of craftsmen (shirkat al-sana'i') and explain why the Hanafi school permits it even when trades and places differ.

Core Idea
A craftsman partnership is valid if the work is jointly accepted and halal, even if trades and places differ.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the partnership of craftsmen (shirkat al-sana'i'). Unlike capital partnerships, this form relies on labor and agency. The Hanafi school rules it valid under specific conditions, offering flexibility that other schools may not allow. We will unpack those conditions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that shirkat al-sana'i' is a distinct form of partnership where artisans jointly accept work. Its ruling according to the Hanafi school is ja'iz (permissible) and sahih (valid) when conditions are met.
The text explicitly calls it 'ja'iz'.
2
List the essential conditions
From the passage, extract the conditions: joint acceptance of work (al-taqabbal), the work must be halal, profit sharing must be agreed upon, and no corrupt conditions that invalidate the partnership.
Unity of trade or place is NOT a condition.
3
Examine the underlying cause (maqsad)
The text states that the purpose is acquisition through mutual agency. Since agency is permissible, the partnership is valid. This cause does not require unity of trade or place.
The reasoning is based on the permissibility of wakalah.
4
Apply to the examples given
Consider the examples: a tailor and dyer, two teachers, a fuller with a tool and a partner with a house. All are valid because the work is joint and halal. This shows the scope.
The text also mentions that if one partner provides only tools and the other works, the partnership is fasid.
5
Note the Hanafi position and authority
The mufta bihi position is that the partnership is valid even if one partner does not master the craft. Authorities cited include al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Sadr al-Shahid.
The text also notes an intra-Hanafi discussion on whether it can be mufawada or 'inan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتقبل إن اشترك خياطان أو خياط وصباغ على أن يتقبلا الأعمال ويكون الكسب بينهما بالرفع عطف على مفاوضة» بيان لشركة الصنائع، وظاهره أن التقبل والوجوه غير المفاوضة والعنان وقدمنا خلافه وفي البزازية وشركة التقبل والوجوه قد تكون مفاوضة وعناناً فالعنان ما يكون في تجارة خاصة، والمفاوضة ما تكون في كل التجارات اهـ. وسيأتي بيان فائدة كونها مفاوضة وإنما جاز هذا النوع من الشركة لأن المقصود منه التحصيل وهو ممكن بالتوكيل لأنه لما كان وكيلاً في النصف أصيلاً في النصف تحققت الشركة في المال المستفاد وأفاد بقوله أو خياط وصباغ أنه لا يشترط فيه اتحاد العمل. قالوا : ولا يشترط أيضاً اتحاد المكان لأن المعنى المجوز لها وهو ما ذكرنا لا يتفاوت، فالمراد من قوله إن اشترك خياطان صانعان ولو حكماً، اتحد عملهما أو اختلف بعد أن يكون عملاً حلالاً يمكن استحقاقه فشمل ما إذا اشترك معلمان لحفظ الصبيان وتعليم الكتابة والقرآن فإن المختار جوازه كما في البزازية، وما إذا كان له آلة القصارة ولآخر بيت اشتركا على أن يعملا في بيت هذا على أن يكون الكسب بينهما فإنه جائز، وكذا سائر الصناعات ولو من أحدهما أداة القصارة والعمل من الآخر فسدت والربح للعامل وعليه أجرة مثل الأداة ؛ كذا في البزازية وفي القنية : اشترك ثلاثة من الجمالين على أن يملأ أحدهم الجوالق ويأخذ الثاني فمها ويحملها على الثالث فينقله إلى بيت المستأجر والأجر بينهم بالسوية فهي فاسدة. قال رضي الله عنه : فسادها لهذه الشروط فإن شركة الحمالين صحيحة إذا اشترك الحمالون في التقبل والعمل جميعاً، ولو اشتركا في تقبل كتب الحجاج على أن ما رزقهما الله تعالى فيه فبينهما نصفان فهذه شركة جائزة .اهـ. وقلنا ولو كان حكماً ليشمل ما إذا اشتركا في صنعة ولم يحسنها أحدهما فإنها صحيحة كما سيأتي . وقيدنا بكون العمل حلالاً لما البيري في حاشية الأشباه في الوديعة قوله : (قال رضي الله عنه فسادها لهذه الشروط) قال الرملي : قدم أنها لا تفسد بالشروط الفاسدة. وفي البزازية الشركة تبطل ببعض الشروط الفاسدة حتى لو شرط التفاضل في الوضيعة لا تبطل الشركة وتبطل باشتراط عشرة لأحدهما والظاهر أنها لا تبطل بأكثر الشروط .اهـ. وبه يحصل الجواب تأمل. قوله: (وقلنا ولو كان حكماً ليشمل الخ) قال في النهر : لا حاجة إليه إذ المشترك فيه إنما هو العمل لا خصوص الخياطة ولذا قالوا : من صور
His statement: (And it is accepted if two tailors, or a tailor and a dyer, partner on the condition that they both accept work and the earnings be between them) – with 'raf' it is conjuncted to 'mufawada'. This is an explanation of partnership of craftsmen. Its apparent meaning is that 'acceptance and credit' is other than 'mufawada' and 'inan', and we have previously presented its opposite. In al-Bazzaziyyah: The partnership of acceptance and credit may be mufawada or 'inan. 'Inan is what is in a specific trade, and mufawada is what is in all trades. The benefit of it being mufawada will be explained later. This type of partnership is permissible because the purpose of it is acquisition, which is possible through agency. Since he is an agent in half and a principal in half, the partnership is realized in the earned property. And his statement 'or a tailor and a dyer' indicates that unity of work is not required. They said: Unity of place is also not required because the reason permitting it, which we have mentioned, does not vary. So the meaning of his statement 'if two tailors partner' is two craftsmen, even if de facto (hukman), whether their work is the same or different, provided that the work is halal and can be earned. This includes if two teachers partner to teach children writing and Quran, for the chosen view is that it is permissible, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And if one has a fuller's tool and the other has a house, and they partner to work in this house with the condition that the earnings be between them, it is permissible. Similarly for all crafts. If one provides the fuller's tool and the other does the work, the partnership is corrupt (fasid), and the profit belongs to the worker, and he must pay the rental value of the tool. This is in al-Bazzaziyyah. In al-Qunyah: Three camel drivers partnered on the condition that one fills the sack, the second takes its mouth, and the third carries it to the customer's house, and the wage is divided equally among them; this is corrupt. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: Its corruption is due to these conditions, for the partnership of porters (hammalin) is valid if the porters partner in acceptance and work together. And if two partner in accepting the books of pilgrims on the condition that whatever Allah grants them from it be divided in half, this is a valid partnership. We said: 'even if de facto (hukman)' to include the case where they partner in a craft and one does not master it; it is valid, as will come. We restricted it to halal work because of al-Bayri in his commentary on al-Ashbah on the chapter of deposit. His statement: (Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: Its corruption is due to these conditions) – al-Ramli said: He previously stated that it is not corrupted by corrupt conditions. In al-Bazzaziyyah: The partnership is invalidated by some corrupt conditions; even if a condition of inequality in loss is stipulated, the partnership is not invalidated, but it is invalidated by stipulating a fixed amount (ten) for one of them. Apparently it is not invalidated by most conditions. Contemplate this for a proper answer. His statement: (And we said 'even if de facto' to include ...) – al-Nahr said: There is no need for it, since what is shared is the work, not specifically tailoring. That is why they said: Among its forms...
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage discusses the partnership of craftsmen (shirkat al-sana'i'). It is a form of partnership where two or more artisans agree to jointly accept work and share the earnings. The text clarifies several key points: First, this type of partnership is distinct from mufawada (full mutual partnership) and 'inan (limited partnership), but it can also take those forms depending on the scope. Second, it is valid even if the craftsmen have different trades (e.g., tailor and dyer), because the underlying cause (maqsad) is earning through mutual agency, which does not require unity of trade. Similarly, unity of place is not required. Third, the work must be halal and capable of being claimed as earnings. Examples include two teachers teaching children, a fuller providing and a partner providing a house, etc. If one supplies the tool and the other performs the work, the partnership is corrupt (fasid) because the tool contribution is not labor; the worker gets the profit but must pay rent for the tool. Fourth, the text gives an example from al-Qunyah of three camel drivers whose partnership is corrupt due to the division of tasks (each doing a specific task), because true partnership requires joint acceptance and work. The correct form is for all to accept and perform the work collectively. Fifth, the passage addresses corrupt conditions: not all invalidate the partnership. For example, a condition for unequal loss does not invalidate, but stipulating a fixed profit for one partner does. Finally, it is permissible even if one partner does not master the craft, because the partnership is based on the work being done, not on individual skill. The author notes that some later scholars like al-Bayri and al-Ramli provided refinements on this topic.

Key Terms
شركة الصنائع (shirkat al-sana'i'): Partnership of craftsmen, where artisans jointly accept work and share earnings, without necessarily contributing capital.
التقبل (al-taqabbal): Acceptance of work orders; the act of taking on a job from a customer.
الحكم (al-hukm): De facto; here, 'even if de facto' means even if one partner does not actually perform the craft himself, it is valid as long as the work is done by someone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT required for a valid shirkat al-sana'i' according to the Hanafi school?
A) The work must be halal.
B) All partners must practice the same craft.
C) The partners must jointly accept work.
D) The profit sharing must be agreed upon.

Key Takeaway
A craftsman partnership is valid in the Hanafi school as long as work is jointly accepted, halal, and profit sharing is agreed; unity of trade or place is not required.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
10 min
Corrupt Conditions and Invalid Scenarios in Shirkat al-Sana'i'
Explains corrupt conditions and invalid examples in craftsman partnerships

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which conditions corrupt a shirkat al-sana'i' and apply the rulings to scenarios like the camel driver example and tool-labor partnerships.

Core Idea
Not all corrupt conditions invalidate the entire partnership; some only affect the condition, while others void the contract.

This lesson examines the corrupt (fasid) scenarios and conditions in craftsman partnerships. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides key examples, including the camel drivers' division of tasks and the case where one partner provides only tools. We will learn how to distinguish between conditions that invalidate the partnership and those that merely require adjustment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the corrupt scenarios in the text
The passage gives two clear examples: (1) Three camel drivers dividing tasks individually (fill sack, tie mouth, carry) – this is fasid. (2) One partner provides a tool, the other works – the partnership is fasid and the worker must pay tool rental.
Both show that the partnership must involve joint work, not divided tasks or passive contribution.
2
Understand the principle behind corruption
The corruption arises because the partnership does not involve true joint acceptance and work. The camel drivers are working separately in sequence, not together. The tool provider is not contributing labor, only capital.
The text says 'its corruption is due to these conditions' – the conditions here refer to the division of labor.
3
Distinguish between types of corrupt conditions
The text notes that some corrupt conditions invalidate the partnership (like fixing a profit amount) while others do not (like stipulating unequal loss). The partnership is invalidated only by certain conditions.
Al-Ramli and al-Bazzaziyyah are cited for this nuance.
4
Apply the rule to the camel driver example
The partnership of three camel drivers is corrupt because they divided the work into separate tasks. The correct form is that all accept the work and perform it collectively.
The valid example: two partners accepting pilgrims' books and sharing earnings.
5
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
The mufta bihi: conditions that prevent joint work or assign fixed profit invalidate the partnership. Conditions like unequal loss do not invalidate. The partnership remains valid but the condition is void.
This is important for drafting partnership agreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتقبل إن اشترك خياطان أو خياط وصباغ على أن يتقبلا الأعمال ويكون الكسب بينهما بالرفع عطف على مفاوضة» بيان لشركة الصنائع، وظاهره أن التقبل والوجوه غير المفاوضة والعنان وقدمنا خلافه وفي البزازية وشركة التقبل والوجوه قد تكون مفاوضة وعناناً فالعنان ما يكون في تجارة خاصة، والمفاوضة ما تكون في كل التجارات اهـ. وسيأتي بيان فائدة كونها مفاوضة وإنما جاز هذا النوع من الشركة لأن المقصود منه التحصيل وهو ممكن بالتوكيل لأنه لما كان وكيلاً في النصف أصيلاً في النصف تحققت الشركة في المال المستفاد وأفاد بقوله أو خياط وصباغ أنه لا يشترط فيه اتحاد العمل. قالوا : ولا يشترط أيضاً اتحاد المكان لأن المعنى المجوز لها وهو ما ذكرنا لا يتفاوت، فالمراد من قوله إن اشترك خياطان صانعان ولو حكماً، اتحد عملهما أو اختلف بعد أن يكون عملاً حلالاً يمكن استحقاقه فشمل ما إذا اشترك معلمان لحفظ الصبيان وتعليم الكتابة والقرآن فإن المختار جوازه كما في البزازية، وما إذا كان له آلة القصارة ولآخر بيت اشتركا على أن يعملا في بيت هذا على أن يكون الكسب بينهما فإنه جائز، وكذا سائر الصناعات ولو من أحدهما أداة القصارة والعمل من الآخر فسدت والربح للعامل وعليه أجرة مثل الأداة ؛ كذا في البزازية وفي القنية : اشترك ثلاثة من الجمالين على أن يملأ أحدهم الجوالق ويأخذ الثاني فمها ويحملها على الثالث فينقله إلى بيت المستأجر والأجر بينهم بالسوية فهي فاسدة. قال رضي الله عنه : فسادها لهذه الشروط فإن شركة الحمالين صحيحة إذا اشترك الحمالون في التقبل والعمل جميعاً، ولو اشتركا في تقبل كتب الحجاج على أن ما رزقهما الله تعالى فيه فبينهما نصفان فهذه شركة جائزة .اهـ. وقلنا ولو كان حكماً ليشمل ما إذا اشتركا في صنعة ولم يحسنها أحدهما فإنها صحيحة كما سيأتي . وقيدنا بكون العمل حلالاً لما البيري في حاشية الأشباه في الوديعة قوله : (قال رضي الله عنه فسادها لهذه الشروط) قال الرملي : قدم أنها لا تفسد بالشروط الفاسدة. وفي البزازية الشركة تبطل ببعض الشروط الفاسدة حتى لو شرط التفاضل في الوضيعة لا تبطل الشركة وتبطل باشتراط عشرة لأحدهما والظاهر أنها لا تبطل بأكثر الشروط .اهـ. وبه يحصل الجواب تأمل. قوله: (وقلنا ولو كان حكماً ليشمل الخ) قال في النهر : لا حاجة إليه إذ المشترك فيه إنما هو العمل لا خصوص الخياطة ولذا قالوا : من صور
His statement: (And it is accepted if two tailors, or a tailor and a dyer, partner on the condition that they both accept work and the earnings be between them) – with 'raf' it is conjuncted to 'mufawada'. Key Terms
الشروط الفاسدة (al-shurut al-fasidah): Conditions that corrupt (invalidate) the partnership, such as stipulating a fixed profit for one partner.
الجمالين (al-jamalayn): Camel drivers; in the text, three camel drivers who divide tasks.

Checkpoint
Which of the following conditions does NOT invalidate a shirkat al-sana'i' according to the Hanafi school?
A) Stipulating that one partner gets a fixed profit of 10 dinars.
B) Stipulating that losses are shared unequally.
C) Dividing the work into sequential tasks (e.g., one loads, one drives).
D) One partner provides only tools and the other does all the work.

Key Takeaway
In shirkat al-sana'i', not all corrupt conditions invalidate the partnership; conditions that prevent joint work or fix profits do, but conditions like unequal loss do not.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate

Ruling on Partnership Based on Work (Shirkat al-A'mal)
States the basic ruling of shirkat al-a'mal and lists invalid types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of shirkat al-a'mal, distinguish valid from invalid forms, and explain the permissibility of unequal profit division.

Core Idea
Shirkat al-a'mal is valid when partners accept lawful work and share earnings, but invalid for haram or non-owing work.

This lesson examines the partnership based on work without capital (shirkat al-a'mal) as explained in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The passage clarifies that such a partnership is valid, each partner's acceptance binds both, and profit division can be unequal. It also lists invalid types, such as partnership in haram work or in activities where no fee is owed, like humming recitations or begging. The goal is to understand the core conditions and common invalid scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
The passage first affirms that a partnership without capital is valid: work accepted by one partner binds both, and earnings are shared.
This is the foundation of shirkat al-a'mal.
2
Recognize invalid types
The passage cites al-Bazzaziyyah, al-Qunyah, and al-Zahiriyyah to list invalid partnerships: haram work, brokers' work (fee not owed), recitation with humming (no fee owed), and begging (agency invalid).
The common element: the work must be such that a fee is legitimately owed.
3
Understand the flexibility of the contract
The phrase 'that they accept the works' is not restrictive. Various forms are valid, e.g., one accepts goods and the other works, or one cuts and the other sews.
The partnership can involve different tasks and still be valid.
4
Analyze profit division
Profit can be divided equally or unequally even if the less skilled partner receives more. The correct view is permissibility because profit is based on guarantee (daman) of work, not on the essence of the work.
This is a key distinguishing feature of the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشركة بينهما وكل ما يتقبله أحدهما يلزمهما وكسب أحدهما بينهما ووجوده إن اشتركا بلا مال في البزازية : لو اشتركا في عمل حرام لم يصح .اهـ. وقيدنا بإمكان استحقاقه لما في القنية : ولا تجوز شركة الدلالين في عملهم ولا شركة القراء في القراءة بالزمزمة في المجلس لأنها غير مستحقة عليهم ولا شركة السؤال لأن التوكيل بالسؤال لا يصح. ولما في الظهيرية : ولو أن ثلاثة من القراء اشتركوا في المجلس والمعازي بالزمزمة والألحان فهذه الشركة فاسدة لأن ما اشتركوا فيه لا يكون مستحقاً عليهم ولا على أحدهم ..اهـ. وقوله «على أن يتقبلا الأعمال» ليس بقيد لأنهما لو اشتركا على أن يتقبل أحدهما المتاع ويعمل الآخر أو يقبل أحدهما المتاع ويقطعه ثم يدفعه إلى الآخر للخياطة بالنصف جاز، كذا في القنية لكن من شرط عليه العمل فقط لو تقبل جاز فلو شرط على الصانع أن لا يتقبل وإنما عليه العمل فقط لا يجوز لأنه عند السكوت جعل إثباتها اقتضاء ولا يمكن ذلك مع النفي؛ كذا في المحيط . وشمل قوله والكسب بينهما ما إذا شرطاه على السواء أو شرطا الربح لأحدهما أكثر من الآخر، وقد صرح به في البزازية معللاً بأن العمل متفاوت وقد يكون أحدهما أحذق، فإن شرطا الأكثر لأدناهما اختلفوا فيه .اهـ. والصحيح الجواز لأن الربح بضمان العمل لا بحقيقته ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي القاموس : وقد قبل به كنصر وسمع وضرب قبالة وقبلت العامل العمل تقبلاً نادر، والاسم القبالة وتقبله العامل تقبيلاً نادر أيضاً اهـ.
Book of Partnership. What one of them accepts of work binds both, and the earnings of one are between them and exist if they partner without capital. In al-Bazzaziyyah: If they partner in haram work, it is not valid... We restricted it to the possibility of entitlement because in al-Qunyah: The partnership of brokers in their work is not permitted, nor the partnership of reciters in recitation with humming in the gathering because it is not owing to them, nor the partnership of beggars because agency for begging is not valid. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If three reciters partner in the gathering and condolences with humming and melodies, this partnership is invalid because what they partnered in is not owing to them nor to any of them... His statement 'that they accept the works' is not a restriction because if they partner such that one accepts the goods and the other works, or one accepts the goods and cuts them then gives them to the other for sewing in half, it is permissible, as in al-Qunyah. But if the condition is only on him to work, if he accepts, it is permissible; but if he conditions on the artisan not to accept and he only works, it is not permissible because at silence it establishes it as implied and that cannot be with negation... His statement 'and the earnings between them' includes whether they condition it equally or they condition more profit for one, as stated in al-Bazzaziyyah reasoning that work varies and one may be more skilled. If they condition more for the lesser, there is disagreement. The correct is permissibility because profit is by guarantee of work not by its essence... In al-Qamus: 'qabila bihi' like 'nasara' etc., and 'qabalta al-'amal taqabbulan' rare, the noun 'qibalah' and 'taqabbulahu al-'amal taqbil an' rare also.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling of shirkat al-a'mal (partnership based on work without capital). It states the foundational ruling: when two or more people form a partnership without capital to accept work, any work accepted by one partner binds both, and the earnings are shared between them according to their agreement. The author then clarifies exceptions by citing later Hanafi works: partnering in haram activity is invalid; partnership of brokers is invalid because their brokerage fee cannot be legitimately owed; partnership of reciters humming in gatherings is invalid as no fee is owed; partnership of beggars fails because agency for begging is invalid. However, if they partner such that one accepts goods and the other works, or one cuts and the other sews, it is valid. The condition 'that they accept the work' is not restrictive; various valid forms exist. The passage also rules that profit division may be unequal, based on the guarantee of work, and the correct view is permissibility. The author quotes lexical references from al-Qamus.

Key Terms
شركة الأعمال (shirkat al-a'mal): A partnership where partners contribute no capital but agree to accept work and share earnings, each liable for work accepted by the other.
تقبل (taqabbul): Accepting work (as a contractor) on behalf of the partnership.
مستحق (mustahiq): Owing; a fee or payment that is legally claimable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a partnership formed to engage in haram work?
A) It is permissible (ja'iz) if both agree.
B) It is invalid (lam yasihh) per al-Bazzaziyyah.
C) It is valid but makruh.
D) It depends on the type of haram work.

Key Takeaway
Shirkat al-a'mal is valid for lawful work that is mustahiq, and profit division can be unequal based on agreement; the key condition is that work accepted by one binds all partners.
